Why No Separate Refutation?
Author explains his decision not to write a separate refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author chose to reprint his book rather than write a new refutation, and how he categorizes the critic's arguments into three branches.

Core Idea
The best refutation is often the one already written.

In this passage, the author responds to a suggestion that he write a detailed refutation of a critic's book. He explains that upon reviewing the critic's work, he found it to consist of three familiar objections already addressed in his own book. Thus, he decides that simply reprinting his book is sufficient. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and the three branches of criticism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the author's tone and his overall argument that his own book suffices.
The passage is a first-person narrative; focus on the author's decision.
2
Identify the three branches
The critic's book is divided into three branches. Find each one: (1) religion vs. science, (2) predestination and free will with the story of Iblis, (3) dialectical materialism.
These branches are clearly marked with 'As for the first/second/third branch'.
3
Understand why reprinting suffices
The author argues his own book already covers the second branch thoroughly, and the other branches are either already addressed or not worth engaging. Note how he connects the branches to his existing work.
He specifically mentions his experience teaching the topic at university.
4
Note the methodological critique
The author points out that the critic should have used proper hadith criticism (riwaya and sanad) instead of relying on weak traditions and ecstatic utterances. This is a key deficiency he identifies.
This shows the author's commitment to sound methodology.
5
Reflect on the dismissal of materialism
The author simply states he should not occupy himself with dialectical materialism. Consider why he might feel no need to refute it directly.
Perhaps he considers it already refuted by his positive argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد كان من جملة الملاحظات التي وصلتني ، اقتراح أن أضمن الطبعة الثانية من هذا الكتاب رداً علمياً مفصلاً على ذاك الذي كتب يخرف من لبنان ضمن شعارات من ألفاظ العلم واصطلاحاته (۱) ، ثم أبى بعض البسطاء من الناس إلا أن يرفعوه بطريقتهم العجيبة التي انتقدوه بها ، إلى مستوى الباحثين والثائرين والأبطال .. ولقد استعرضت الكتاب ، فوجدته في مجموع بحوثه التي يعرض لها ذا ثلاث شعب أما الشعبة الأولى فحديثه فيها محصور في الكلام المكرر القديم حول الدين والعلم ، وأن النهضة العلمية الجارفة لم تبق في العقل أي مكان للإيمان بالله !.. وأما الشعبة الثانية فقد تناول فيها موضوع الجبر والاختيار والمشيئة والقضاء ، وصور من ذلك مشكلة جسدها في قصة إبليس وأما الشعبة الثالثة والأخيرة فقد تناول فيها عرض ما رأه شرحاً علمياً حقيقياً لقصة هذا الوجود وما فيه ، وهو الشرح المادي الديالكتيكي للتاريخ ولا أظن أن ثمة سبيلاً للرد على الكتاب بشعبه الثلاث هذه ، خيراً من إعادة طبع كتاب « كبرى اليقينيات الكونية » كما هو . . فموضوع الجبر والاختيار - وهو شباك قديم أخرق لا يزال محترفو الإلحاد وهـواتـه يلجؤون إليه - مشروح في كتابنا هذا شرحاً بيناً علمياً مفصلاً ، لم يترك - فيما رأيت من تجربتي مع طلابي في الجامعة - حاجة إلى أي زيادة أو شرح . ولا أحتاج أن أضيف إليه شيئاً للرد على من كتب يخرّف في شعبه الثلاث تلك ، سوى أن أقول له : إن حقائق الجبر والاختيار لا تؤخذ من شطحات الحلاج أو بعض الصوفية أو الأخبار والآثار الموضوعة والضعيفة ، وإنما لنا في السبيل إلى ذلك منهج من البحث العلمي في الرواية والسند كان عليك أن تدرسه قبل ذلك أما موضوع المادية الجدلية ، وشرحه للتاريخ على أساسها ، فما ينبغي أن أشغل بها (۱) هو صاحب كتاب : نقد الفكر الديني
And among the observations that reached me was the suggestion that I include in the second edition of this book a detailed scientific refutation of that one who wrote drivel from Lebanon under slogans of scientific words and terms (1), then some simple people insisted on raising him, in their strange way of criticizing him, to the level of researchers, revolutionaries, and heroes.. And I reviewed the book, and I found it in its total research that it presents has three branches: As for the first branch, his speech in it is confined to the old repeated talk about religion and science, and that the sweeping scientific renaissance has left no place in the mind for faith in God!.. And as for the second branch, he addressed in it the topic of predestination and free will, the will and decree, and images of that including the problem embodied in the story of Iblis. And as for the third and last branch, he addressed in it presenting what he considered a true scientific explanation of the story of this existence and what is in it, which is the dialectical materialist explanation of history. And I do not think there is a way to refute the book in its three branches better than reprinting the book 'Kubra al-Yaqiniyyat al-Kawniyyah' as it is. So the topic of predestination and free will - and it is an old worn-out window that professionals of atheism and its amateurs still resort to - is explained in our book with a clear, scientific, detailed explanation that did not leave - in what I saw from my experience with my students at the university - any need for any addition or explanation. And I do not need to add anything to refute the one who wrote drivel in those three branches, except to say to him: The truths of predestination and free will are not taken from the ecstatic utterances of al-Hallaj or some Sufis or fabricated and weak reports and traditions, rather we have in the way to that a methodology of scientific research in transmission (riwaya) and chain of narration (sanad) that you should have studied before that. As for the topic of dialectical materialism and its explanation of history on its basis, I should not occupy myself with it. (1) He is the author of the book 'Critique of Religious Thought'.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is the author's response to a suggestion that he write a detailed refutation of a book from Lebanon that criticizes religious thought. The author explains that he reviewed that book and found it has three branches: (1) old arguments about religion and science claiming science leaves no room for faith, (2) the issue of predestination and free will using the story of Iblis, and (3) dialectical materialism as the explanation of existence. The author argues that the best refutation is to reprint his own book 'Kubra al-Yaqiniyyat al-Kawniyyah' as it is, because it already addresses these topics thoroughly. He specifically notes that the topic of predestination and free will is already explained in detail, and he has no need to add anything except to point out that his critic should have used proper methodology of hadith criticism rather than relying on weak traditions. Finally, he dismisses the need to engage with the dialectical materialism topic. The footnote identifies the critic as the author of 'Critique of Religious Thought'.

المادية الجدلية
شعب ثلاث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the author is ignoring the criticism or avoiding a direct response.
Correction: The author shows he has carefully reviewed the critic's work and concludes that his own book already refutes it, so a separate response is unnecessary.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the best way to refute the three branches of the Lebanese book?
A) Write a new book
B) Reprint his own book as it is
C) Ignore it
D) Write a short article

Key Takeaway
The author's existing comprehensive book already refutes the critic's three branches, so reprinting it suffices; he adds only a methodological critique on hadith criticism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows the author refusing to engage with dialectical materialism because it is not worth his time. Are there doubts or criticisms about your faith that you entertain, even though they are based on weak foundations? What will you do today to stop giving them your mental energy and instead focus on solid knowledge?
?
The author emphasizes that truths about predestination and free will are not taken from weak sources like ecstatic Sufi sayings or fabricated hadith. When you form your beliefs on this topic, do you rely on sound, verified sources? List one source you will study to ensure your understanding is correct.
?
If someone challenged your faith using the same three branches as the critic, would you be able to respond with a 'book' of solid knowledge, like the author had? What is one area you need to strengthen so that you are not dependent on others to defend your faith? Commit to studying it this week.

Defending the Use of Philosophy and Logic in Kalam
Buti defends mutakallimun against accusations of corrupting tawhid by using philosophy and logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the early mutakallimun used philosophical tools in their defense of tawhid.

Core Idea
Kalam used philosophy not to corrupt tawhid, but to defend it against heretics.

In this footnote, Buti addresses a modern criticism that theologians corrupted tawhid by using philosophy and logic. He argues that the science of kalam was developed as a defensive response to heretics who themselves used philosophical arguments. The mutakallimun had to engage with their opponents on their own terms.

Guided Path
1
Understand the accusation
Some researchers today claim that the mutakallimun corrupted tawhid by amassing rules of philosophy, logic, and debate in their works, instead of simply following the Quran's method.
2
Recognize the defensive purpose
Buti argues that kalam was not authored for those with strong faith, but for heretics (zanadiqa) and aberrant sects who used philosophical doubts and mental pretensions.
The primary audience of kalam was not the faithful, but the doubters.
3
Understand the dilemma
The mutakallimun faced a choice: remain silent and let falsehood spread, or confront the heretics using their own tools to expose their sophistry.
They chose confrontation out of necessity for the Islamic call.
4
Apply the same logic to modern doubts
Buti asks whether we can avoid engaging with modern ideologies like dialectical materialism or existentialism using their own methods, or if we can simply present the Quran to those who don't recognize its value.
The method remains the same: engage with opponents using arguments they accept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أجل هذا لا نرى عدلاً ما يقول بعض الباحثين اليوم من أن علماء الكلام أفسدوا صفاء التوحيد بما حشدوا في بحوثهم عنه من قواعد الفلسفة ومبادئ المنطق وأصول الجدال ، وأنه كان يغنيهم عن ذلك اتباع منهج القرآن وعرض براهينه . يقول : ليس عدلاً أن يقال عنهم شيء من هذا الكلام، وذلك لأن صحة علم الكلام لم تؤلف شيء من أجل أمن السؤال واستضاء القلب سراجه ، وإنما ألفت لزنادقة اتكؤوا في زندقتهم على شبه فلسفية ، وفرق مارقة اتكأت في شذوذها على تكلفات عقلية ، وكانوا ( رحمهم الله ) بين أن يسكتوا عن لغو أولئك الزنادقة وفيقهة هؤلاء المتنطعين فيشيع في الناس أمرهم ويتسع إلى العقول الغافلة طريقهم ، وبين أن يتصدوا لهم فيكشفوا عن زيف شبههم وسفسطة أدلتهم وفساد طريقتهم ، فلم يترددوا في أن يؤتروا الثاني على الأول استجابة لما تقضي به ضرورة الدعوة الإسلامية ولما هو معروف من حكم الله في ذلك ولا يضير صحيح هذا الجواب أن كثيراً من تلك الشبه والإشكالات ، لا مكان لها اليوم حيال ما استجد من شبه وسفسطات أخرى ، صحيح إنما نتحدث عن مسوغات ما فعله أولئك الأسلاف في عهدهم. ومع ذلك فالسبيل واحدة والمنهج لا يختلف وإن اختلفت أنواع الشبه والخداع، فهل لنا أن نقول اليوم، حيال ما استجد من شبه الفلسفة المادية الديالكتيكية أو الفلسفة الوجودية أو لوثة التطور والارتقاء وانتخاب الأصلح : لسنا بحاجة أن ندحض سفسطة أرباب هذه الشبه بأدلة العلم وبراهينه التي يرعم أرباب هذه الشبه أنفسهم أنهم يتمسكون بها ؟ وهل يصح لنا أن نقول : يكفينا أن نعرض لهم منهج القرآن وهم لا يعلمون ما هو القرآن وما هي قيمته الذاتية ؟!
For this reason, we do not see as just what some researchers today say, that the theologians (mutakallimun) corrupted the purity of monotheism (tawhid) by what they amassed in their researches about it from the rules of philosophy, principles of logic, and fundamentals of debate, and that it would have sufficed them to follow the method of the Qur'an and present its proofs. He says: It is not just to say anything of this kind about them, because the soundness of the science of kalam was not authored for anything like assurance from questioning and the heart's lamp being lit; rather it was authored for heretics who relied in their heresy on philosophical doubts, and for aberrant sects who relied in their deviation on mental pretensions. And they (may God have mercy on them) were between remaining silent about the nonsense of those heretics and the understanding of these arrogant extremists, so that their affair would spread among the people and their path would widen to heedless intellects, and between confronting them and exposing the falsehood of their doubts, the sophistry of their arguments, and the corruption of their way. So they did not hesitate to prefer the second over the first, in response to what the necessity of the Islamic call and what is known of God's judgment in that regard require. And the correctness of this answer is not harmed by the fact that many of those doubts and problems have no place today regarding new doubts and other sophistries. Correct, we are only talking about the justifications for what those predecessors did in their era. Nevertheless, the path is one and the method does not differ, even if the types of doubts and deception differ. Can we say today, regarding new doubts like dialectical materialism, existential philosophy, or the contamination of evolution and progress and survival of the fittest: we do not need to refute the sophistry of the proponents of these doubts with the proofs of science and its evidences which the proponents of these doubts themselves claim to adhere to? And can it be correct for us to say: it suffices us to present them with the method of the Qur'an while they do not know what the Qur'an is and what its intrinsic value is?!
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a footnote that constitutes a defense of the mutakallimun against contemporary criticism. Buti argues that the accusation of corrupting tawhid by using philosophy and logic is unjust. He states that the science of kalam was not written for those who already have faith and assurance, but for heretics and aberrant sects who used philosophical doubts and mental pretensions. The mutakallimun had two options: remain silent (allowing falsehood to spread) or confront the doubters using their own tools. They chose the latter out of necessity. Buti then applies the same logic to modern doubts, asking whether we can avoid engaging with them using arguments acceptable to their proponents. The passage ends with rhetorical questions highlighting the futility of simply presenting the Qur'an to those who do not recognize its authority.

Key Terms
علماء الكلام
توحيد
زنادقة
فرق مارقة
سفسطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the mutakallimun introduced philosophy into Islam unnecessarily, corrupting tawhid.
Correction: The author shows that their use of philosophy was a defensive measure against heretics who already used philosophical arguments.

Checkpoint
According to the footnote, for whom was the science of kalam primarily authored?
A) For ordinary believers to strengthen their faith
B) For heretics and aberrant sects who used philosophical doubts
C) For Greek philosophers
D) For the general public

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimun's use of philosophy and logic was a necessary defensive response to heretical challenges, not an innovation that corrupted tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter an atheist argument based on materialism or evolution, do you dismiss it by saying 'the Quran is enough' without truly understanding their premises? Are you willing to learn their arguments so you can refute them effectively, just as the mutakallimun did with the heretics of their time?
?
Have you ever silently ignored a modern doubt (like existentialism or survival of the fittest) because engaging with it feels too difficult or intimidating? What would it cost you to confront it head-on, using the tools of reason and evidence that its proponents respect?
?
If you were accused of corrupting the purity of tawhid by using logic or philosophy in defending your faith, would you have the courage to continue, knowing that your intention is to protect the truth rather than dilute it? What does your answer reveal about your commitment to the Islamic call?

Critique of Jumpers and Their Caricature of Religion
Buti criticizes pseudo-philosophers and describes their distorted view of religion's origins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's critique of pseudo-philosophers who lack rigorous method and distort the nature of religion.

Core Idea
True knowledge requires rigorous method, not leaps of imagination.

Buti challenges those who claim expertise in philosophy yet abandon all method, leaping to conclusions based on imagination. He exposes their caricature of religion as a historical evolution from soothsaying to prophethood. This lesson examines his critique and the stark contrast they draw between science and belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage Carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice Buti's tone of astonishment and his repetition of 'astonishing'.
The passage is dense; reading it twice helps.
2
Identify the Two Main Criticisms
First, Buti criticizes their lack of method—they jump to conclusions. Second, he criticizes their mislabeling: they call their jumping 'science' and label Muslim methodology as mere 'belief'.
3
Examine the Caricature of Religion's History
According to these 'jumpers', religion began with soothsaying and astrology, progressed to magic, then to prophethood—which appropriated traditions and claimed sanctity. Understand each stage.
This is a distorted view, contrasting with the actual teachings.
4
Reflect on the Contrast
Contrast their view with how Buti describes true religion: taught by prophets, believers, and based on proofs. The jumpers dismiss it as mere 'belief'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعجيب حقاً أن نجد ثلة ممن درسوا من كل فن جانباً ثم زعموا أنهم تخصصوا في الفلسفة والمنطق وطرائق البحث - يفصلون القول في كثير من حقائق العقيدة عن الأنبياء واليوم الآخر كما يتخيلون ويحبون ، دون أن يركبوا إلى شيء من ذلك متن أي طريقة في البحث ، بل تجدهم يقفزون إلى ذلك قفزاً وقد أغمضوا أعينهم وأفكارهم ، فما يدري أحدهم أهو ينحط في متاهات من الجهل أم وسط ساحات من التخيل والحدس !..
والأعجب ، أن تجدهم فوق ذلك ، يعبرون عن قفزهم هذا ( بالعلم ) .. ويعبرون عن منطلق المسلمين ومنهجيتهم ( بالاعتقاد ) !.. فالدين في حقيقته العلمية عند هؤلاء ( الوثابين ( سلسلة فكرية بدأت في عصورها الأولى بالكهانة والتنجيم ، ثم ترقت إلى السحر ، ثم إلى النبوة التي امتصت كثيراً من التقاليد والإحيائيات فجعلت لها قداسة روحية معينة . أما الدين كما يعلمه أنبياؤه والمؤمنون به والباحثون في أدلته وبراهينه فهو قائم على مجرد ( الاعتقاد ) !..
And it is truly astonishing that we find a group who have studied a bit of every art and then claimed to have specialized in philosophy, logic, and methods of research - they elaborate on many truths of creed concerning the prophets and the Last Day as they imagine and wish, without mounting any method of research for any of that; rather, you find them jumping to that, having closed their eyes and minds, so that none of them knows whether he is descending into labyrinths of ignorance or into arenas of imagination and conjecture! And what is even more astonishing, you find them beyond that, calling this jumping 'science'... and calling the starting point of Muslims and their methodology 'belief'! So religion in its scientific reality according to these 'jumpers' is a series of thought that began in its early ages with soothsaying and astrology, then progressed to magic, then to prophethood which absorbed many traditions and revivals and gave them a certain spiritual sanctity. As for religion as taught by its prophets, believers, and researchers of its proofs and evidences, it is based on mere 'belief'!
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a sharp critique of a certain class of intellectuals who claim to have studied philosophy and logic but lack any rigorous method. Buti describes them as 'jumpers' (al-waththābīn) who leap to conclusions about religious doctrines—such as prophethood and the afterlife—based on their own imagination and desire, without following any structured inquiry. They close their eyes and minds, and do not know if they are lost in ignorance or in fantasy. Even more astonishing, they label their own leaps 'science' while labeling the Muslim approach as mere 'belief'. Buti then summarizes the distorted view of religion that such 'jumpers' hold: according to them, religion evolved from soothsaying and astrology to magic to prophethood, which they see as absorbing earlier traditions and claiming spiritual authority. In contrast, the actual religion as understood by its prophets, believers, and scholars is dismissed by them as mere 'belief'. The commentary follows Buti's progression: first the astonishment at their lack of method, then their mislabeling of science and belief, then their historical caricature of religion.

Key Terms
الوثابين (al-waththābīn): the jumpers
قفز (qafz): jumping
تخيل (takhayyul): imagination
حدس (ḥads): conjecture
كهانة (kihānah): soothsaying
تنجيم (tanjīm): astrology

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Buti is opposing all philosophical inquiry.
Correction: Buti is only opposing those who claim philosophy but lack method and misrepresent religion.

Checkpoint
What term does Buti use to describe those who jump to conclusions without method?
A) المستشكلون (al-mustashkilūn)
B) الوثابون (al-waththābūn)
C) المدافعون (al-mudāfiʿūn)
D) الملحدون (al-mulḥidūn)

Key Takeaway
Method and rigor are essential for valid inquiry; dismissing religion as mere belief is a distortion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself jumping to a conclusion about a religious matter without properly investigating its evidence? What was the result, and how can you commit to a more rigorous approach starting today?
?
The jumpers label their own leaps as 'science' and dismiss Muslim methodology as mere 'belief'. In what area of your life might you be doing the same—calling your own assumptions 'knowledge' while discounting others' careful study as 'just faith'?
?
When has your imagination or desire led you to close your mind to a truth that contradicted it? What would it take for you to open your eyes and submit to evidence, even if it is uncomfortable?

Avoiding Ambiguous Historical Disputes
Author advises avoiding ambiguous Mu'tazila disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author advises avoiding engagement with certain historical theological disputes between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunnah.

Core Idea
Some disputes are too ambiguous to affect faith — focus on clear evidence.

The author continues outlining his methodological principles. He now addresses how to handle the many historical disputes between the Mu'tazila and Sunni majority. His advice is practical and based on the nature of the evidence: when the proofs are ambiguous and the outcome does not determine belief, it is better to avoid unnecessary polemics.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the author gives two reasons for avoiding these disputes: ambiguity of evidence and irrelevance to contemporary faith.
The passage begins with 'ثانياً' indicating it is the second methodology.
2
Understand the first reason: ambiguity
The author says these disputes involve evidence that has ambiguity (شبهة) and probability (احتمال), so being certain of one view does not lead to disbelief.
This means the evidence is not clear-cut enough to declare one side as disbelief.
3
Understand the second reason: irrelevance
He adds that these disputes do not relate to any doubt in faith for people today. Therefore, they are not a priority.
The author is concerned with present-day faith, not historical polemics.
4
Apply the principle
Consider how this principle guides a teacher or student of Islam: focus on issues that are clear and affect contemporary belief, and avoid endless debates on ambiguous matters.
This is a practical methodology for prioritizing theological study.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانياً.
·
- عدم التوغل في كثير من الخلافات التي قامت بين المعتزلة وجمهور المسلمين من أهل السنة والجماعة ، إذ هي أمور لا ينتهي الجزم فيها بأحد القولين إلى الكفر ، لقيام الشبهة والاحتمال في أدلتها ؛ ثم هي . في ذلك أن نتبنى ما اتفق عليه جمهور المسلمين من أهل السنة والجماعة بعد معرفة الدليل
لا تتعلق بأي شبه في الإيمان لأي فئة من الناس اليوم . فحسبنا
والبرهان.
Second: Not delving into many of the disputes that arose between the Mu'tazila and the majority of Muslims from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, for they are matters in which being certain of one of the two sayings does not lead to disbelief, due to the presence of ambiguity and probability in their evidences; then they do not relate to any doubt in faith for any group of people today. So it is sufficient for us in that to adopt what the majority of Muslims from Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah have agreed upon, after knowing the evidence and the proof.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is the second methodological principle. The author commits to avoiding extensive engagement with historical disputes between the Mu'tazila and the Sunni majority. He argues that these are matters where holding either view does not lead to disbelief (kufr) because the evidence is ambiguous and probabilistic. Moreover, these disputes do not affect contemporary faith. Therefore, it is sufficient to adopt the consensus of the Sunni majority after understanding the evidence, without delving into the details of the debates.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
أهل السنة والجماعة
جمهور المسلمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the author dismisses all theological discussions with the Mu'tazila as useless or wrong.
Correction: The author only avoids disputes where the evidence is ambiguous and the outcome does not affect fundamental faith. He does not reject all discussions, only those that are inconclusive and irrelevant.

Checkpoint
Why does the author avoid delving into disputes with the Mu'tazila?
A) Because he agrees with the Mu'tazila
B) Because those disputes do not lead to disbelief and are not relevant today
C) Because they are too difficult to understand
D) Because he is a Sunni and rejects all their views

Key Takeaway
The author advises against delving into ambiguous historical disputes that have no bearing on contemporary faith, focusing instead on clear evidence and consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there theological debates you get caught up in that do not affect your faith or practice? Will you now deliberately set them aside and trust the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah?
?
When you encounter an ambiguous historical dispute, do you feel pressured to pick a side? How can you apply the author's advice to adopt the majority view after knowing the evidence?
?
This passage says some disputes are irrelevant to current doubts in faith. Is there a dispute you are holding onto that distracts you from more important matters of belief and action? What concrete step will you take to let it go?

Critique of Blind Imitation and Islam's Rationality
Buti criticizes blind imitation and affirms Islam's rational methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's critique of two groups: European 'scientists' who oppose religion from bias, and Muslims who blindly imitate European interpretations, and you will see how Buti asserts that Islam's creedal principles are based on a precise, rational methodology.

Core Idea
Blind imitation of Europe distorts Islam; true Islam is inherently rational.

After establishing the supremacy of sound intellect, Buti now tackles a practical problem: the blind adoption of European attitudes toward religion. He identifies two groups—European 'scientists' whose opposition to religion stems from partisanship, and Muslims who mimic European interpretations without critical thought. This passage sets the stage for Buti's positive claim that Islam itself follows a rigorous scientific method, free from bias and blind imitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups criticized
Read the passage and note the two distinct groups Buti criticizes: the European 'scientists' (العلميون) and the Muslim imitators who are 'pale shadows' of Europe.
Buti first describes the Europeans' motives, then turns to the imitators.
2
Understand the European 'scientists'
Buti says they refute only their own tradition's religion, not the true religion (Islam). Their opposition is driven by European partisanship and fear of Muslim resurgence.
They are not genuine seekers of truth.
3
Understand the Muslim imitators
These Muslims adopt European categories (positive/doctrinal vs. negative/scientific interpretations) and apply them to Islam mechanically, seeking complete imitation.
Buti calls them 'pale shadows'—they lack original thought.
4
Grasp Buti's dismissal and conclusion
Buti dismisses both groups as irrelevant to the truth-seeker. He then affirms that Islam's creedal principles follow a precise, honest scientific method guided solely by intellect, free from partisanship or blind imitation.
This is the positive thesis: Islam is rational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصحيح . ولكنهم اكتفوا من مقتضيات العقل الصحيح بتفنيد الدين الذي عندهم وتأويله حسب ما يتخيلون ويرون ، دون أن يلتفتوا إلى الدين الحق الذي يسجد العقل والعلم لكل مبادئه وأحكامه فقد صدهم عن ذلك شعور آخر هو شعور العصبية والذاتية الأوربية والحذر المستمر من أن يعود المسلمون مرة أخرى إلى سيادة العالم ، كما كانوا كذلك ذات يوم ، فأطلق على هؤلاء اسم ) العلميين . ثم إنك تعلم أن في العرب والمسلمين أناساً ، تحسبهم أناسي ينطقون ويعقلون ويتكلمون ، وهم في الحقيقة ليسوا إلا ظلالاً شاحبة ممتدة تتحرك بحركات أوربا وأفكار أوربا وفلسفة أوربا . فهؤلاء الناس رأوا أن الدين في أوربا له تفسيران : تفسير إيجابي هو في حقيقته تفسير اعتقادي محض ، وتفسير سلبي هو ، كما يسمونه هناك ، تفسير علمي محض . فجاؤوا بهذين التفسيرين من هناك وأطلقوهما على الدين الإسلامي هنا ، لا لشيء ، ولكن لمجرد أن يتكامل الظل ويأتي التقليد محكماً من سائر أطرافه . فهذا هو السبب العميق لهذه الظاهرة العجيبة عند هؤلاء الناس . وليس يهمنا إطلاقاً أمر هذا الصنف من الناس ، بعد أن يعلم العاقل المتأمل الحر ، من كل ما أوضحته في هذا التمهيد ، أن الإسلام لا يعني تلك المعتقدات التي خاصمت أوربا العقل في سبيلها ، وأن الإسلام يقوم في مبادئه الاعتقادية كلها على منهج علمي دقيق نزيه لا تخطه إلا يد العقل وحده دون أن يكون ثمة سلطان لعصبية أو رغبة في اعتقاد أو تقليد واتباع
The correct. But they were satisfied from the requirements of sound intellect with refuting the religion they have and interpreting it according to what they imagine and see, without turning to the true religion, before which intellect and knowledge prostrate for all its principles and rulings. Another feeling turned them away from that: the feeling of European partisanship and subjectivity, and the constant caution that Muslims might once again return to world dominance, as they were one day. So these were called 'the scientists' (al-`ilmiyyin). Then you know that among Arabs and Muslims there are people whom you count as human beings speaking, reasoning, and talking, but in reality they are only pale extended shadows moving with the movements of Europe, the ideas of Europe, and the philosophy of Europe. These people saw that religion in Europe has two interpretations: a positive interpretation which in reality is a purely doctrinal interpretation, and a negative interpretation which is, as they call it there, a purely scientific interpretation. They brought these two interpretations from there and applied them to the Islamic religion here, for no reason, but merely so that the shadow might be complete and imitation might come firmly from all its sides. This is the profound reason for this strange phenomenon among these people. And it does not concern us at all regarding this class of people, after the free reflective rational person knows, from all that I have clarified in this introduction, that Islam does not mean those beliefs which Europe's intellect fought in its cause, and that Islam in all its creedal principles stands upon a precise, honest scientific method that nothing traces except the hand of the intellect alone, without any authority of partisanship or desire in belief or imitation and following.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and critique of two groups: first, the European 'scientists' (العلميون) who distort religion based on a flawed view of reason; second, those Muslims who blindly imitate Europe. The author begins by stating that the 'scientists' limit themselves to refuting their own tradition's religion, not the true religion (Islam), which reason and knowledge fully submit to. Their opposition is driven by European bias and fear of Muslim resurgence. He then describes a class of Muslims who are mere shadows of Europe, adopting European interpretations of religion (positive/doctrinal and negative/scientific) and imposing them on Islam. This mimicry, he argues, is the deep cause of the strange phenomenon. However, the author dismisses this group, asserting that the true seeker will see from the introduction that Islam is not like the beliefs Europe fought; rather, its creedal principles follow a precise, honest rational methodology free from partisanship or blind imitation.

Correction: Buti clarifies that Islam's creedal principles are based on a precise scientific method guided by pure intellect, not partisanship or blind tradition.

Checkpoint

B) Partisanship and fear of Muslim resurgence

Key Takeaway
Buti asserts that true Islam follows a precise, rational scientific method, unlike the biased opposition of European 'scientists' or the blind imitation of their Muslim mimics.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself defending Islam in intellectual settings, do you rely on Allah's guidance and the rational proofs of the tradition, or have you absorbed the embarrassment of the modern world? Are you willing to study the 'precise, honest scientific method' of Islam so that you can testify to its truth with confidence?
?
Buti says the European scientists were driven by 'partisanship and fear' rather than sound intellect. When you question an Islamic ruling or practice, is your heart free from hidden partisanship—whether for a particular scholar, a cultural trend, or the desire to appear modern? Will you ask Allah to purify your motives before you speak?
?
Many Muslims unknowingly become 'pale shadows' of the West, adopting its frameworks uncritically. What specific worldview or assumption from your education or media have you accepted without measuring it against the Qur'an and Sunnah? Today, will you commit to examining one such idea in light of Islam's rational methodology?

The True Cause of Sectarian Division: Transgression, Not Ignorance
Author identifies transgression as cause of sectarian divergence despite prophetic knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the primary cause of sectarian division after the prophets was not a lack of knowledge but transgression and envy among people.

Core Idea
Sectarian division stems from moral failure, not from insufficient revelation.

This lesson examines a key argument about the origin of sectarian splits. The author contends that people did not divide because they lacked clear guidance; rather, they had knowledge but chose to deviate out of transgression. We will explore the evidence and the Quranic verse that supports this claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author sets up a contrast between what would have happened if people followed the prophets and what actually happened.
Pay attention to the word 'بغياً' – it is the key to the argument.
2
Identify the cause of division
Find the specific phrase that identifies the cause. The passage uses 'بغياً بينهم' – transgression/envy among themselves.
3
Reflect on the Quranic verse
The author cites Quran 3:19. Reflect on how this verse supports the point that division occurred after knowledge came, out of transgression.
The verse also includes a warning about disbelief.
4
Consider the misconception
Many assume that sectarian differences arise from unclear or insufficient revelation. The passage challenges this assumption. Ask yourself: What does this imply about human responsibility?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيما بعث بـه ، وما كانوا ليتفرقوا إلى عقائد متباينة مختلفة ، ولكنهم اختلفوا وتفرقوا فيما بينهم ، واختلقوا على الأنبياء ، ما لم يقولوه على الرغم مما جاءهم من العلم في ذلك ، بغياً بينهم . وصدق الله العظيم إذ يقول في محكم تبيانه : إنَّ الدِّينَ عِندَ الله الإسلام ، وما اختلف الذين أوتوا الكتاب إلا مِنْ بَعدِ ما جَاءَهُمُ العِلمُ بَغْياً بينَهُمْ ومَن يكفُرُ بآيات الله فإنَّ اللهَ سَريعُ الحساب ) [ آل عمران : ١٩ ]
In what he was sent with, and they would not have separated into diverse conflicting creeds, but they differed and divided among themselves, and they invented lies against the prophets, [attributing to them] what they did not say, despite the knowledge that came to them concerning that, out of transgression among themselves. And Allah the Almighty spoke the truth when He said in the precise exposition of His revelation: 'Indeed, the religion in the sight of Allah is Islam. And those who were given the Scripture did not differ except after knowledge came to them, out of transgression among themselves. And whoever disbelieves in the verses of Allah, then indeed Allah is swift in account.' [Al-Imran: 19]
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents an argument about the origin of sectarian division. The author states that if people had followed what the prophets brought, they would not have separated into diverse conflicting creeds. However, they did differ and divide among themselves, and even attributed falsehoods to the prophets despite having received clear knowledge. The cause of this division is identified as 'بغياً' (transgression/envy) among them. The author then cites Quran 3:19 to reinforce the point: that those who received Scripture only differed after knowledge came to them, out of transgression. The verse also warns that disbelief in Allah's signs will be swiftly judged. Thus, the passage emphasizes that division is not due to lack of evidence but due to moral failure—transgression and mutual envy.

Key Terms
بغياً (transgression/envy)
اختلقوا (they invented lies)
العلم (knowledge)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sectarian divisions arise from insufficient or unclear revelation.
Correction: The passage argues that people had clear knowledge (العلم) from the prophets, but they divided out of transgression (بغياً), not ignorance.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary cause of sectarian division after the prophets?
A) Lack of clear knowledge
B) Transgression and envy among people
C) Differences in the prophets' messages
D) The passage does not specify a cause

Key Takeaway
Sectarian division after the prophets was caused by transgression and envy, not by a lack of divine guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you disagree with another Muslim on a matter of creed, do you catch yourself feeling a sense of superiority or even envy? Ask yourself: is my reaction driven by a desire for truth, or by transgression (بغياً)? What would it take to purify my intention today?
?
The passage says people invented lies against the prophets out of transgression. Have you ever twisted a teaching of Islam to support your own group or opinion, even slightly? If so, how can you repent and commit to speaking only what you know to be true, even if it humbles you?
?
Knowledge came to them, yet they transgressed. Is there an area of Islamic knowledge that you are aware of, but you ignore or resist because it would require you to change or admit fault? What step will you take this week to act on that knowledge instead of turning away?

The Irrational Core of Materialist Philosophy
Author condemns materialism as intellectually dishonest and states its core doctrine.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's characterization of materialist philosophy as the most obstinate form of atheism and its central claim about matter and the clash of opposites.

Core Idea
Materialism, claiming matter as the ultimate origin, is fundamentally opposed to reason.

The author identifies the most extreme form of atheism: materialist philosophy. He describes its core claim that matter is the origin of everything and that all cosmic phenomena arise from the conflict of opposites. This lesson unpacks that claim and the author's condemnation of it as irrational.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage describing materialism
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the strong language: 'أوغل في المكابرة والمخاصمة للعقل' (most deeply entrenched in obstinacy and opposition to the mind).
Notice that the author does not present this neutrally but with condemnation.
2
Identify the core claim of materialism
Find the sentence that states materialism's claim about matter and the process of cosmic manifestations.
The claim is that matter is the origin and that opposites clash to produce the universe.
3
Reflect on the phrase 'يذهب الآخر جفاء'
Consider the imagery of the inferior going to waste like froth. What does this imply about the author's view of materialism?
This foreshadows the author's critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكنك لا تجد في أنواع الإلحاد أوغل في المكابرة والمخاصمة للعقل من النوع الذي يقوم على الفلسفة المادية التي تزعم أن المادة هي أم الوجود وأبوها وأن جميع مظاهر الكون إنما تنبعث وتتصاعد عن طريق تلاقي المتناقضات وتقارعها ، حيث يتغلب الأفضل ويذهب الآخر جفاء !.. فلسفة نمت وهي وترعرعت يوماً ما في جهة من جهات العالم ، ثم إنها خبت وذوت واضمحلت وتقوض بناؤها الفكري الذي كانت قد أقيمت فيه ، ولم يبق إلا هيكل سياسي مجرد يمسكها وتمسكه : يمسكها لتكون الركن المثبت له وتمسكه ليكون البوق المؤيد لها وهذه الفلسفة محجوجة - على كل حال - بكل تلك البراهين التي ذكرناها ثم هي محجوجة بعد ذلك بأوضح المسلمات البدهية التي تقوم على معارضتها ومخاصمتها : ونحن نناقش هذه الفلسفة في كلا فرعيها المعروفين عند أربابها باسم : - المادية الجدلية - المادية التاريخية ونبدأ بمناقشة الفرع الأول منها فنقول :
But you will not find among the types of atheism any more deeply entrenched in obstinacy and opposition to the mind than the type that is based on materialist philosophy, which claims that matter is the mother and father of existence, and that all manifestations of the universe only arise and emerge through the meeting and clashing of opposites, where the superior prevails and the other goes to waste!... A philosophy that grew and flourished once in a region of the world, then it faded, withered, and vanished, and its intellectual structure on which it was built collapsed, and nothing remained except a mere political framework that holds it and it holds: it holds it to be its supporting pillar and it holds it to be its supporting trumpet. And this philosophy is refuted – in any case – by all those proofs that we have mentioned, and it is also refuted by the clearest axiomatic truths that stand in opposition and contention to it: And we will discuss this philosophy in both of its branches known to its adherents as: - Dialectical Materialism - Historical Materialism. And we begin by discussing the first branch, saying:
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is an introduction and critique of materialist philosophy. The author states that materialism is the most obstinate and mind-opposing form of atheism. He describes its claim: matter is the origin of all, and all cosmic phenomena arise from the conflict of opposites, where the best survives. Then he remarks on its historical decline: although it once flourished, its intellectual structure collapsed, leaving only a political skeleton that supports it and is supported by it. The author then asserts that this philosophy is already refuted by the previously mentioned proofs and by clear axiomatic truths. He then announces his plan to discuss both branches of materialism: dialectical and historical, starting with the first.

Correction: Actually, the author uses highly charged language to condemn materialism as irrational and obstinate.

C) Matter is an illusion.
D) Matter is eternal but not the origin.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Decline of Materialism and Refutation Plan
Author recounts materialism's historical collapse and outlines refutation plan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's account of materialism's intellectual collapse and his plan to refute its two branches.

Core Idea
Materialism's intellectual structure collapsed, leaving only a political framework, and it is refuted by clear proofs.

Having condemned materialism's irrational claim, the author now describes its historical fate: it once flourished but its intellectual structure crumbled, leaving only a political skeleton. He then declares that it is already refuted by earlier proofs and axiomatic truths, and announces his plan to discuss dialectical and historical materialism.

Guided Path
1
Read the historical narrative
Read the Arabic passage about the rise and fall of materialism's intellectual structure. Note the verbs: نمت (grew), خبت (faded), ذوت (withered), اضمحلت (vanished), تقوض (collapsed).
The author uses a series of verbs to emphasize complete decay.
2
Identify what remains
Find what remained after the intellectual collapse: a mere political framework (هيكل سياسي مجرد). Understand the relationship: the framework holds the philosophy and vice versa.
This suggests materialism survives only as a political tool.
3
Understand the refutation claim
The author says materialism is refuted by previous proofs and by axiomatic truths. Identify the two sources of refutation.
The author does not give details here, but references earlier arguments.
4
Note the plan for discussion
The author names the two branches: dialectical materialism and historical materialism. He will start with the first.
This sets up the subsequent lessons.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Materialism's intellectual structure collapsed. What intellectual structures in your own life might be hollow and supported only by convenience rather than truth? Are you holding onto beliefs that have no solid foundation? Commit to examining one belief you hold and testing it against clear proofs.
?
The author says materialism is refuted by axiomatic truths. Are there truths so obvious that you have ignored them because they conflict with your desires? What axiomatic truth about God's existence have you perhaps pushed aside? Today, write down one such truth and ask yourself why you resist it.
?
Materialism survived only as a political tool. Are there aspects of your faith that you maintain only for external reasons—family, community, status—rather than genuine conviction? What would it take for your faith to be intellectually and spiritually alive?

The Marxist Theory of Historical Materialism
Buti states the Marxist theory of historical materialism prior to critiquing it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the basic claims of historical materialism as presented by Buti prior to his critique.

Core Idea
The means of production drives all of human society and history.

Before critiquing historical materialism, Buti faithfully summarizes its central doctrines. This passage lays out how Marxists view the relationship between economics and all aspects of society. It is important to grasp this accurately before evaluating the critique that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the exposition carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that this is Buti presenting the Marxist view, not his own belief.
2
Identify the foundational claim
What does historical materialism say is the ultimate cause of all social phenomena? Locate the phrase 'وسيلة الإنتاج' (means of production).
This is the key causal factor.
3
Understand the denial of absolute truth
Notice that the passage explicitly rejects absolute truth, replacing it with 'developing relativity'. Knowledge is said to be a product of economic conditions.
4
Trace the dialectical process
Follow the stages: flourishing of means of production → capital inflation → seeds of revolution → transfer to proletariat → class struggle → communism.
The process is driven by internal contradictions.
5
Recognize the final outcome
The passage ends with the cessation of conflict and the establishment of communism. This is the ultimate goal of history according to this theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن المقصود بهذا العنوان دعوى أن تركيب المجتمع الإنساني بما فيه القيم المختلفة والأفكار واللغة والمعارف ، كل ذلك ناشئ عن الوضع الاقتصادي الذي نشأ هو بدوره عن سبب الأسباب كلها ، ألا وهو « وسيلة الإنتاج » وعلى هذا فإن الحقيقة المطلقة » لا مكان لها في الوجود كله ، وإنما يمتد في مكانها وعلى اتساع الوجود كله قانون « النسبية المتطورة » في كل شيء ، إذ المعرفة ذاتها وليد ظروفها الاقتصادية ، فمن أين تأتي الحقيقة المطلقة ؟ ثم يزعمون أن تركيب المجتمع الإنساني يتطور تحت سلطان الوضع الاقتصادي ووسيلة الإنتاج ، تطوراً ديالكتيكياً ، أي بعوامل من داخله تحمل بذور نقيضه ، وليس بواسطة عوامل من خارجه كما هو شأن العلة مع المعلول . فازدهار وسيلة الإنتاج يسبب تضخم رأس المال وهذا الوضع نفسه يحمل في طواياه بذور الثورة عليه إذ يتسبب عنه انتقال وسائل الإنتاج إلى طبقة البروليتاريا ، ويستمر هذا التناقض بين وسائل الإنتاج وعلاقات الملكية عاملاً وحيداً للصراع داخل المجتمع . ويظل هذا الصراع مستمراً حتى تنمحي الطبقية من المجتمع إلى الأبد ويدخل العالم في مرحلة الشيوعية العظمى ، وعندئذ يهدأ الصراع وتسكن العاصفة وينتهي كل شيء.
What is meant by this title is the claim that the composition of human society, including its various values, ideas, language, and knowledge, all of that arises from the economic situation which itself arose from the cause of all causes, namely the 'means of production'. And upon this, there is no place for 'absolute truth' in all of existence, but rather in its place and throughout the expanse of all existence extends the law of 'developing relativity' in everything, since knowledge itself is the offspring of its economic circumstances, so from where would absolute truth come? Then they claim that the composition of human society develops under the authority of the economic situation and the means of production, dialectically, that is, by factors from within it that carry the seeds of its opposite, and not by means of factors from outside it, as is the case of cause with effect. So the flourishing of the means of production causes the inflation of capital, and this very situation carries within its folds the seeds of revolution against it, as it causes the transfer of the means of production to the proletariat class. And this contradiction between the means of production and property relations continues as the sole factor of conflict within society. And this conflict continues until class disappears from society forever and the world enters the stage of great communism, and then the conflict calms and the storm settles and everything ends.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the Marxist doctrine of historical materialism, presented by the author in order to refute it. It begins by defining the core claim: that all aspects of human society—values, ideas, language, knowledge—are products of the economic situation, which itself is ultimately determined by the 'means of production'. Consequently, absolute truth is denied; instead, everything is governed by a law of 'developing relativity', since knowledge itself is conditioned by economic factors. The passage then explains the dialectical mechanism of societal development: change comes from internal contradictions (the seeds of the opposite within each stage), not from external causes. It describes the process: the flourishing of the means of production leads to capital accumulation, which generates internal contradictions that result in revolution and transfer of means of production to the proletariat. This class struggle continues until classes are abolished and communism is achieved, at which point conflict ends. The author is faithfully presenting this view before subjecting it to criticism.

شيوعية

Misconception: Buti is endorsing historical materialism.
Correction: Buti is faithfully presenting the Marxist view in order to refute it.

Key Takeaway
Historical materialism claims that the means of production determines all aspects of society and that society develops dialectically through internal contradictions towards communism.

?

?
The theory claims that history will end in a classless utopia. But as a Muslim, you believe in an afterlife and a final judgment. How does the promise of communism compare to the Islamic promise of Jannah? Which one demands more of your current life and why?

Refutation of Economic Determinism: A Historical Counterexample
Buti presents a conditional refutation of economic determinism using historical examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti uses the historical timing of revolutions to disprove the claim that economic prosperity necessarily triggers revolution.

Core Idea
Economic determinism fails because revolutions ignite in poor countries, not rich ones.

Buti presents a powerful objection to the materialist view that economic conditions alone drive historical change. Using the concrete examples of Russia and China, he shows that revolutions occurred where the economy was weak, not strong. This challenges the very foundation of economic determinism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the conditional structure and the vivid imagery of the 'fuse of revolution'.
The passage is a single logical argument; try to follow its flow.
2
Identify the conditional premise
Buti begins with a hypothetical: if economic prosperity and capital accumulation trigger revolution, then revolutions should occur first in wealthy countries. Identify this 'if...then...' statement.
This is the economic determinist claim that he intends to refute.
3
Observe the historical counterexample
Buti contrasts the predicted outcome with actual history: revolutions appeared in Russia and China, not in Sweden, America, or Western Europe. Note the economic conditions of Russia and China at that time – weak and backward.
This is the key evidence that falsifies the premise.
4
Understand the logical conclusion
Because the predicted outcome did not occur, the premise must be false. Buti reinforces this with the imagery of the revolution's fuse igniting where it should not and sleeping where it should.
The argument is a classic modus tollens: if P then Q, not Q, therefore not P.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider what this refutation means for the materialist view of history. Does it deny any role for economics? No, it only denies that economics is the sole determinant.
This connects to the common misunderstanding addressed in the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣ - لو صح أن ازدهار الاقتصاد وتضخم رأس المال هو الذي يقدح زناد الثورة ويسبب انتقال وسائل الإنتاج إلى البروليتاريا ، لاستلزم ذلك أن تقوم هذه الثورة في سويسرا وأمريكا ودول أوربا الغربية قبل ظهورها في أي بقعة أخرى من العالم . ولكنها بدلاً من أن تظهر هناك ، ظهرت في روسيا والصين وفي عهد كان الاقتصاد فيه ضعيفاً ومتخلفاً. لقد انقدح زناد الثورة حيث كان ينبغي أن لا ينقدح ، ونامت عواملها نوماً مستمراً إلى يومنا هذا حيث كان ينبغي أن تستيقظ.
3. If it were true that economic prosperity and capital accumulation are what ignite the fuse of revolution and cause the means of production to be transferred to the proletariat, then it would necessitate that this revolution should occur in Switzerland, America, and Western European countries before appearing in any other part of the world. But instead of appearing there, it appeared in Russia and China at a time when the economy was weak and backward. The fuse of revolution was ignited where it should not have been ignited, and its factors slept continuously until this day where they should have been awake.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the materialist claim that economic factors determine historical change. Buti presents a conditional proof: if the economic determinist premise were true (that prosperity and capital accumulation trigger revolution), then revolutions should have first occurred in wealthy Western countries. However, history shows that revolutions occurred in poor, backward countries like Russia and China, while the prosperous West remained stable. Therefore, the premise is false. He reinforces this with the vivid image of the revolution's fuse igniting where it should not and sleeping where it should be active.

Key Terms
بروليتاريا
وسائل الإنتاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Buti denies any role for economics in historical change.
Correction: Buti only denies that economics is the sole determinant; he does not deny that economic factors play some role.

Checkpoint
What empirical evidence does Buti use to refute economic determinism?
A) The fact that revolutions occurred in Switzerland and America
B) The fact that revolutions occurred in Russia and China, not in wealthy countries
C) The fact that animals did not develop thought
D) The fact that reason is self-contradictory

Key Takeaway
Buti refutes economic determinism by demonstrating that revolutions occur in economically backward countries, not prosperous ones.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Buti shows that the revolution's fuse ignited where it should not, and slept where it should be awake. In your own life, where is the fuse of your iman sleeping—where are you spiritually stagnant despite having every blessing (health, wealth, comfort) that should awaken it? What worldly distraction has drugged that spark, and what is one concrete action you will take this week to fan it into flame?
?
If you truly believe that Allah governs history and not economic forces, how would that change your daily attitude toward your work, your ambitions, and your worries about the future? What is one area of your life where you are acting as if 'economics determines everything,' and how will you realign that with tawheed before you sleep tonight?

The Self-Contradiction of Dialectical Materialism
Buti exposes a contradiction in dialectical materialism's claim about reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how dialectical materialism refutes itself by denying absolute truths while relying on reason to assert an absolute truth.

Core Idea
A system that denies absolute truth cannot claim its own truth is absolute.

Buti now turns to a powerful internal critique of dialectical materialism. Instead of attacking it from outside, he shows that the theory's own claims about reason and truth lead to a contradiction. This lesson unpacks that self-refutation, revealing why materialism cannot consistently ground its own worldview.

Guided Path
1
State the materialist claim
Read the first part of the passage where Buti outlines the materialist view: that reason is a product of economic struggle and absolute truths are illusions.
Notice that this claim reduces all knowledge to relative, time-bound conditions.
2
Follow the implication
If the claim is true, then dialectical materialism itself is just another relative 'truth' — not a universal law. Buti makes this point explicitly.
This is the first half of the contradiction: the theory undermines its own universality.
3
Identify the contradiction
The core contradiction is that materialism denies the intellect's ability to reach absolute truth, yet uses the same intellect to claim the absolute truth of dialectics. Find the sentence where Buti states this clearly.
This is the climax of the argument: a clear logical inconsistency.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Ask yourself: why is this contradiction fatal? How does it show that dialectical materialism cannot be a consistent philosophical system?
This connects to the broader theme of the necessity of absolute truths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ - إن فرضية الدياليكتيك تستلزم القول بأن العقل وما يتبعه من النشاطات الفكرية ليس إلا ثمرة لصراع الإنسان من أجل رفع مستواه الاقتصادي ، وتطوير وسائل الإنتاج ، ومن ثم فإن الحقائق المطلقة أمور نسبية لا وجود لها في ظل المادية التاريخية ، وهي ليست أكثر من ظلال لمقتضيات زمنية متطورة . فإذا فرضنا أن هذا الكلام صحيح ، فإنه لدليل بدهي على أن الدياليكتيك ليس قانوناً حقيقياً يستوعب التاريخ كله ويغطي أطوار الإنسانية كلها ، بل هو ليس إلا كبقية « الحقائق » المزعومة الأخرى ، أمر نسبي لا حقيقة ثابتة له . إن من التناقض الذي لا يخفى على عاقل ، أن نقول بأن أحكام العقل ليست حقائق مطلقة ثابتة ، ثم نعتمد على أحكام العقل ذاته في استنباط ما ندعي أنه أعظم حقيقة ثابتة تستوعب التاريخ الإنساني كله.
4. The hypothesis of dialectics necessitates the claim that the intellect and its accompanying intellectual activities are nothing but the fruit of man's struggle to raise his economic level and develop the means of production, and therefore absolute truths are relative matters that have no existence under historical materialism, and they are no more than shadows of evolving temporal necessities. If we assume that this statement is true, then it is a self-evident proof that dialectics is not a real law that encompasses all history and covers all stages of humanity, but rather it is like all other alleged 'truths', a relative matter with no fixed reality. It is a contradiction not hidden from any rational person to say that the judgments of the intellect are not fixed absolute truths, and then rely on the very judgments of the intellect to deduce what we claim is the greatest fixed truth that encompasses all human history.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of dialectical materialism by exposing a self-contradiction. Buti first states the materialist claim: reason and intellectual activities are mere byproducts of economic struggle, so there are no absolute truths, only relative ones. Then he draws the implication: if that claim is true, then dialectics itself is merely a relative 'truth' with no fixed reality, not a universal law of history. But the real contradiction is highlighted in the final sentence: materialism claims that the intellect's judgments are not absolute truths, yet it relies on the very intellect to deduce what it claims is the greatest absolute truth (the dialectical law of history). This is a logical inconsistency that any rational person can see.

Key Terms
حقائق مطلقة
مادية تاريخية
أحكام العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Buti is rejecting reason itself or arguing that reason cannot be trusted.
Correction: Buti is not rejecting reason; he is exposing that materialism inconsistently uses reason while denying its capacity for absolute truths. His argument defends reason's ability to know absolute truths.

Checkpoint
What is the core contradiction that Buti points out in dialectical materialism?
A) It claims reason is a product of economics but not of biology
B) It denies absolute truths yet uses reason to assert the absolute truth of dialectics
C) It supports revolution in poor countries but not in rich ones
D) It says animals lack thought but humans have it

Key Takeaway
Dialectical materialism refutes itself because it must use reason to assert a universal truth while simultaneously denying that reason can know any absolute truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a worldview that claims all truths are relative while still insisting that your own view is correct? Reflect on a specific instance where you might have done this. How does Buti's exposure of this contradiction challenge you to be more consistent in your beliefs?
?
When you reason about matters of faith, do you ever doubt the reliability of your intellect because of secular critiques? Buti shows that such doubt is self-defeating. How can you trust your intellect as a gift from Allah while avoiding the materialist error?
?
Buti's argument relies on the intellect to expose a contradiction. Do you personally rely on reason in your faith, or have you ever felt that reason and faith are in conflict? What would you say to someone who claims that faith requires abandoning reason?

Two Misguided Views and Reason's Proper Stance
Buti refutes existentialist and pantheist views and states reason's limited role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti refutes two extreme philosophical views about God—existentialist abstraction and pantheist identification—and establishes reason's limited but crucial role.

Core Idea
Two wrong paths: empty abstraction or pantheist confusion; reason knows its limits.

Buti warns that those who speculate without proper methodology fall into either the folly of reducing God to bare existence or the illusion of identifying God with the world. He then presents reason's correct position: reason can prove a necessary being distinct from creation, but it cannot go beyond that to define the relationship between essence and existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation of the two errors
Read the passage carefully to identify the first error of the existentialists (reducing God to empty existence) and the second error of the pantheist Sufis (identifying God with the world).
Notice how Buti uses vivid imagery of an empty vessel vs. a full vessel.
2
Examine reason's response
Look at why reason is presented as the balanced alternative: it affirms a necessary being distinct from contingent things, but refuses to speculate beyond its capacity.
Reason's statement 'I have no concern with that' marks the boundary.
3
Reflect on the lesson's implication
Think about how this passage teaches the proper method of theological inquiry—avoiding extremes and respecting the limits of human understanding.
This connects to the broader theme of reliance on revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجَديرٌ بك إن فعلت ذلك أن تقع إما في الخبل الذي وقع فيه بعض الفلاسفة (الوجوديون) أو في الوهم الذي انجرف فيه بعض الصوفية. فقد زعم أولئك أن حقيقة الله عبارة عن الوجود المجرد عن الماهية التي تشغله وتملؤه، أي إذا سألنــا عن هذا الوجود وجود أي شيء هو؟ فالجواب أنــه ليس وجود أي شيء غير ذاته! أما هؤلاء فقد انتهى بهم الوهم إلى أن حقيقة الله هي وجود العالم نفسه، فهذه الأكوان التي تراها من حولك هي في الحقيقة ليست شيئاً أكثر من وجود الله عز وجل تجسد في هذه الصور والأشكال!.. فانظر إلى ما يفعله الخيال والتأمل الأعزل عن طاقة العقل ومنهجه!.. أولئك تخيلوا وجود الله عز وجل وعاءً فارغاً ليس فيه إلا شيء اسمه الوجـود!.. وهؤلاء تخيلوه وعاء ممتلئاً بكل ماتراه من أصناف المكونات والمخلوقات!. أما العقل، بكل ما يملكه من عدة وبراهين ومناهج للبحث، فإنه يقول: أما وقد ثبت بالبرهان اليقين الذي لاشك فيه أن وجود هذه الممكنات كلها تستند إلى ذات واجبة الوجود تتصف بكل صفات الكمال وتبتعد عن كل صفات النقصان، فلا مندوحة من الإيمان بوجود هذه الذات العظيمة المدبرة لأمر هذا الكون كله وأنها بالضرورة غيره ومستقلة عنه. ولكن ماهي العلاقة بين الذات والوجود، وما الفارق بينهما؟.. يقول العقل في الجواب على هذا: لا شأن لي بشيء من ذلك، لأنـه خـارج عن متناول فهمي وسلطاني. ورحم الله امرءاً عرف حده فوقف عنده (1) لا يحملنك هذا الذي نقول، على أن تقلد بعض الناس فتكفر، أولئك الذين عرفوا بالقول بوحدة الوجود كالشيخ محي الدين بن عربي وعيره. فإن هؤلاء الذين دلت كتبهم على أنهم كانوا يقولون وحدة الوجود، يحتمل أن يكونوا بريئين من هذا المقال وإنما دس ذلك في كتبهم من قبل بعض الزنادقة الذين كانوا يمارسون هذه الخيانة، ويحتمل أن حالاً وجدانية اعترتهم فتاهوا عن الجادة ونطقوا بما لا يعتقدون، وربما اعتقدوه ولكنهم عادوا عنه بعد ذلك. وإذا كانت هذه الاحتمالات كلها قائمة، فإن من الظلم للحقيقة والعدل أن نتجاهلها كلها ونتمسك باحتمال آخر لنسوع بذلك تكفيرهم. ومن المعلوم أنك لو عشت العمر كله لاتقول عن الكافر المتيقن كفره: كافر ـ لم يؤاخذك الله القيامة على ذلك، وأنك لو أطلقت الكفر مرة واحدة في حياتك على من هو عند الله غير كافر، عرضت نفسك للعقاب العظيم من الله عز وجل. فما الموجب، بعد ذلك، لتوزيع ألقاب الكفر على من عرفوا في حياتهم بالإسلام والتقوى وشاع أمرهم بين الناس على ذلك ولا نعلم كيف أبوا إلى ربهم جل جلاله. وحسبك لبيان الحكم وتحذير الناس من التقليد أن نوضح لهم الحق ونفند الباطل ونحذرهم من اتباعه بقطع النظر عن قائله.
And it is fitting that if you do that, you fall either into the folly that some philosophers (the existentialists) fell into, or into the illusion that some Sufis drifted into. For those claimed that the reality of God is merely existence stripped of the quiddity that occupies and fills it, i.e., if we ask about this existence, 'Existence of what is it?', the answer is that it is not the existence of anything other than itself! As for these, the illusion ended with them that the reality of God is the existence of the world itself, so these universes that you see around you are in reality nothing more than the existence of Allah Almighty incarnated in these forms and shapes! So look at what imagination and reflection divested of the power of reason and its methodology do! Those imagined the existence of Allah Almighty as an empty vessel containing nothing but something called existence! And these imagined it as a vessel filled with all the kinds of components and creatures you see! As for reason, with all the means, proofs, and research methodologies it possesses, it says: When it has been established by certain proof, about which there is no doubt, that the existence of all these contingent things rests upon a self-necessary essence characterized by all perfections and free from all imperfections, there is no escape from believing in the existence of this great essence that manages the affair of this entire universe, and that it is necessarily other than it and independent of it. But what is the relationship between the essence and existence, and what is the difference between them? Reason says in answer to this: I have no concern with any of that, because it is beyond the reach of my understanding and authority. May Allah have mercy on a person who knew his limit and stopped at it. (1) Let what we say not lead you to imitate some people and pronounce disbelief (takfir) upon those known for the statement of the unity of existence, like Shaykh Muhyi al-Din ibn Arabi and others. For these people, whose books indicate they used to say the unity of existence, it is possible that they are innocent of this statement and that it was inserted into their books by some heretics who practiced this betrayal, and it is possible that an ecstatic state overcame them so they strayed from the path and uttered what they did not believe, and perhaps they believed it but then recanted afterwards. And since all these possibilities exist, it is an injustice to truth and justice to ignore them all and hold fast to another possibility in order to justify their takfir. It is well known that if you lived your entire life without saying 'unbeliever' about a confirmed unbeliever, Allah would not hold you accountable on the Day of Resurrection for that, whereas if you utter disbelief once in your life about someone who is not an unbeliever in Allah's sight, you expose yourself to great punishment from Allah Almighty. So what compels, after that, to distribute labels of disbelief upon those who were known in their lives for Islam and piety and whose reputation spread among people on that basis, while we do not know how they returned to their Lord, majestic is His glory? It suffices for clarifying the ruling and warning people against blind imitation that we clarify the truth, refute falsehood, and warn them against following it, regardless of who said it.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage refutes two extreme views resulting from improper speculation and presents reason's proper stance, including a footnote cautioning against rash takfir. The author first warns that exceeding the limit in contemplation leads either to the folly of existentialist philosophers who strip God's existence of any quiddity, reducing Him to a bare abstraction, or to the illusion of pantheist Sufis who identify God with the created world. He then contrasts these with the correct position of reason: reason, using its certain proofs, establishes that contingent beings depend on a necessary essence distinct from them. However, when asked about the relationship between essence and existence, reason admits its inability, as that lies beyond its scope. The footnote emphasizes caution in declaring takfir against historical figures like Ibn Arabi who were associated with pantheistic expressions, citing possible forgery, ecstatic utterance, or later repentance, and warns that falsely accusing a Muslim of disbelief is a grave sin. The proper approach is to clarify truth and refute falsehood without targeting individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all philosophical speculation about God is equally valid, or that reason can fully comprehend the divine nature.
Correction: Buti shows that speculation without method leads to extremes, and reason itself acknowledges its limits, affirming that some matters are beyond its grasp.

Checkpoint
In Buti's refutation, what is the error of the existentialists?
A) Identifying God with the world
B) Reducing God to bare existence without attributes
C) Denying God's existence altogether
D) Claiming God is a physical body

Key Takeaway
The correct approach to God is to avoid the extremes of empty abstraction and pantheist identification, and to recognize the proper boundaries of reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you contemplate Allah's nature, do you tend to think of Him as a vague abstraction (like the existentialists) or as somehow part of the world around you (like the pantheists)? Which of these temptations is more present in your heart, and what specific verse or proof will you use to correct it starting today?
?
Reason has shown you its limit: it can affirm that Allah exists and is distinct from creation, but it cannot probe the relationship between His essence and existence. Are you willing to stop at that limit in your own thinking, or do you feel restless trying to understand what Allah has not revealed? What will you do when your mind wants to cross that boundary—will you humble yourself or persist?
?
Buti praises the person who 'knew his limit and stopped at it.' Think of one area in your life—your beliefs, your worship, or your curiosity—where you have not stopped at your limit. What is that area, and what practical step will you take today to stop, submit, and trust Allah's wisdom?

Caution in Declaring Takfir
Buti cautions against rash takfir on figures like Ibn Arabi due to three possibilities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle of caution when declaring takfir on historical figures like Ibn Arabi, due to possibilities of forgery, ecstatic states, or later repentance.

Core Idea
Better to err on the side of mercy than to wrongly accuse a Muslim of disbelief.

After refuting the two misguided views, Buti adds a crucial footnote cautioning against blindly declaring takfir on figures associated with pantheistic statements, such as Ibn Arabi. He lists three possibilities that prevent certainty: the statement may have been forged by heretics, it may have been uttered in an ecstatic state not reflecting true belief, or the person may have later repented. The gravity of false accusation requires restraint, and our duty is to clarify truth rather than judge individuals.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and list the three possibilities
Carefully read the passage and identify the three reasons Buti gives for not jumping to takfir: forgery, ecstatic state, and later repentance.
Notice that Buti emphasizes uncertainty prevents conclusive judgment.
2
Understand the principle of caution
Reflect on the principle that avoiding false accusation takes priority over punishing true disbelief, as shown by the warning that falsely declaring takfir invites great punishment.
Buti contrasts the ease of silence with the gravity of rash speech.
3
Apply the principle to real scenarios
Consider how this principle applies to our attitude towards historical figures and theological controversies: we should clarify truth but not hastily judge individuals.
This aligns with the broader Islamic principle of avoiding harm.
