The Real Dispute Over the Qur'an's Createdness: Terminology, Not Substance
Buti explains the real nature of the dispute over the Qur'an's createdness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the historical dispute between the Mu'tazila and their opponents over the Qur'an's createdness is only about terminology, not about the nature of the Qur'an itself.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila agreed with others: the Qur'an's words are created, its meanings eternal.

Buti aims to clear up a common misconception. Many think the Mu'tazila denied the eternity of the Qur'an entirely, but in reality both sides agreed on the fundamentals. The only disagreement was what to call the eternal meaning. This lesson unpacks that clarification and warns about distortions from Orientalists and their imitators.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp Buti's main claim about the real nature of the dispute.
Notice the rhetorical question at the start; it sets up his argument.
2
Identify the point of agreement
Find the sentence where Buti states that all parties agree the words are created and the meanings are eternal. This is the key foundation.
3
Understand the terminological dispute
Recognize that the only difference is in naming the eternal meaning: is it called the attribute of speech or the attribute of knowledge and will?
This shows the dispute is over labels, not substance.
4
Reflect on Buti's criticism
Consider Buti's critique of Orientalists and Muslims who parrot confusion without reflection. Why does he call their statements 'nonsense'?
He implies that clear thinking reveals the agreement.
5
Connect to your learning
Ask yourself: Why is this clarification important? How does it affect understanding of Islamic theological history?
This prevents falling into simplistic narratives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما علاقة الخلاف الذي بين المعتزلة والآخرين ، بهذه المسألة ، وقد علمت أنهم جميعاً متفقون على أن ألفاظ القرآن حادثة وأن معانيه قديمة وأن خلافهم فقط في تسمية المعنى القديم : هل يسمى صفة الكلام ، أم يسمى صفة العلم والإرادة ؟ .. ثم إنه ليس عجيباً كل العجب أن ترى في المستشرقين أو المبشرين من يفوه بهذا السخف رغم أن في رؤوسهم عقولاً يفكرون بها ، لأنها صنعتهم المعروفة . ولكن العجيب والمضحك حقاً أن تلتفت حولك فتبصر أناساً من العرب المسلمين يتباهون بنفس ذلك السخف ويدندنون بعين ذلك الهراء في نشوة وطرب بالغين دون أن تبصر أي أثر للتأمل والفكر في شيء من كلامهم أو بحوثهم ! .. فمن أجل أن لا تنطلي عليك أي شبهة من كلام كثيرين ممن خاضوا في الحديث عن تاريخ المعتزلة وقضية خلق القرآن وعدمه من أجانب مستشرقين أو مقلديهم من المسلمين - اقتضت الضرورة أن نفصل القول في ذكر حقيقة هذا الخلاف وجوهره ، وأسبابه .
And what is the relation of the disagreement that is between the Mu'tazila and the others to this issue, when you know that they all agree that the words of the Qur'an are created and that its meanings are eternal, and that their disagreement is only in naming the eternal meaning: is it called the attribute of speech, or is it called the attribute of knowledge and will? .. Then it is not at all strange that you see among the Orientalists or missionaries someone who utters this nonsense, even though they have minds in their heads with which they think, because it is their known craft. But the truly strange and laughable thing is that you look around you and see people from Muslim Arabs boasting of the same nonsense and humming the same drivel in great ecstasy and delight, without seeing any trace of reflection or thought in any of their speech or researches! .. So in order that no doubt from the speech of many of those who have waded into talking about the history of the Mu'tazila and the issue of the createdness or uncreatedness of the Qur'an, from foreign Orientalists or their imitators from the Muslims, may deceive you - necessity required that we speak in detail about the reality of this disagreement, its essence, and its causes.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage clarifies the nature of the historical dispute between the Mu'tazila and their opponents over the createdness of the Qur'an. Buti states that both sides agree that the words (alphaz) of the Qur'an are created (haditha) and that its meanings (ma'ani) are eternal (qadima). The only difference is in terminology: whether to call the eternal meaning 'the attribute of speech' (sifat al-kalam) or 'the attribute of knowledge and will' (sifat al-'ilm wa al-irada). He then criticizes Orientalists and missionaries for spreading confusion about this issue, and laments that some Muslims parrot this nonsense without reflection. He concludes by stating his intention to explain the true nature of the disagreement to prevent the reader from being deceived.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think the Mu'tazila denied the eternity of the Qur'an entirely.
Correction: Buti shows they agreed the meanings are eternal; the dispute was only over terminology.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the real point of agreement between Mu'tazila and their opponents regarding the Qur'an?
A) The Qur'an is entirely created.
B) The Qur'an is entirely eternal.
C) The words are created and the meanings are eternal.
D) The dispute is about the nature of God's will.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over the Qur'an's createdness is only about naming the eternal meaning, not about the essence of the Qur'an.

Refutation of Anthropomorphist Interpretation
Critique of anthropomorphists and their misuse of ambiguous texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why anthropomorphists (al-mujassima) err by imposing their imagination on the Quran and ignoring its linguistic and textual nuances.

Core Idea
Anthropomorphists worship mental idols, not the true God revealed in the Quran.

Sanusi here exposes a fundamental misreading of the Quran committed by those who picture God as a body. He shows that such interpretations are not legitimate engagements with the text but rather projections of the mind onto it. This lesson will help you recognize the difference between genuine Quranic exegesis and the distortion of the anthropomorphists.

Guided Path
1
Read the original passage
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the strong language Sanusi uses to describe the anthropomorphists.
2
Identify the key error
Sanusi says the anthropomorphists imagine God as a body and then force Quranic verses to match that image. What are the specific textual and linguistic mistakes they make?
Look for phrases like 'clinging to literal meanings', 'ignoring decisive texts', 'ignoring metaphor and trope'.
3
Understand the Quranic support
Sanusi quotes Quran 3:7. Read the verse in context and see how it condemns following ambiguous texts for discord.
4
Reflect on the main misconception
Some might think anthropomorphists are simply taking the Quran literally. Sanusi argues they are actually ignoring parts of the Quran and the Arabic language. How does this passage clarify the real issue?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعطلة ، أو المجسمة ، وهم الذين تخيلوا الله عز وجل في صورة جسم ، ثم ذهبوا يتخيلون له الشكل والسمت الذي يريدون ، متمسكين بظواهر هذه النصوص ومعرضين عن النصوص القاطعة الأخرى ، ومتجاهلين طبيعة هذه اللغة وما فيها من مجاز واستعارة وأساليب مختلفة في التعبير .

فهؤلاء لا يقام لهم أي حساب فيما يتعلق بكتاب الله تعالى وتفسيره وليسوا من نصوصه - محكمه أو متشابهه - في شيء . وإنما هم قوم تصوروا الذات الإلهية كما صورته أخيلتهم المجردة ، ثم استنهضوا آيات من كتاب الله تعالى إلى تلك الأخيلة لتصدقها وتؤمن لهم بها ، وأنى لآيات الله الباهرة أن تدلّ إلا على الحق المنير ، فعادوا يعكفون على أصنام لهم أقاموها في رؤوسهم بدلاً من أن ينصبوها أمام أعينهم . وليس أصدق في وصف حالهم مما قال الله عز وجل عنهم : ﴿ فَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ فِي قُلُوبِهِمْ زَيْغٌ فَيَتَّبِعونَ ما تَشابَة مِنْهُ ابْتِغاءَ الفِتْنَةِ وابتغاء تأويله ) و آل عمران : ٧]
The Mu'attila (negators) or Mujassima (anthropomorphists) are those who imagined God Almighty in the form of a body, then went on to imagine for Him the shape and aspect they wanted, clinging to the literal meanings of these texts, turning away from other decisive texts, and ignoring the nature of this language and what it contains of metaphor, trope, and various styles of expression. So these people are not taken into account at all regarding the Book of God Almighty and its interpretation, and they have nothing to do with its texts—whether firm or ambiguous. Rather, they are a people who depicted the Divine Essence as their bare imaginations depicted it, then they summoned verses from the Book of God Almighty to those imaginations to confirm them and provide them with belief. But how could God's dazzling verses point to anything but the manifest truth? So they returned to worshipping idols they had erected in their heads instead of placing them before their eyes. Nothing is truer in describing their condition than what God Almighty said about them: 'As for those in whose hearts is deviation, they follow what is ambiguous from it, seeking discord and seeking its interpretation' (Al 'Imran: 7).
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a critique and refutation of two groups: the Mu'attila (those who negate God's attributes) and the Mujassima (those who anthropomorphize God). The author describes how the Mujassima imagined God as having a physical body, then attributed to Him the shape and form they desired. They did this by clinging to the literal meanings (ẓawāhir) of certain ambiguous texts (mutashābihāt) while ignoring other clear and definitive texts (muḥkamāt), and disregarding the Arabic language's use of metaphor, trope, and varied expressions. The author then states that such people have no standing in matters of interpretation of God's Book; they are not really dealing with its texts at all. Instead, they formed a mental image of God from their pure imaginations, then forced Quranic verses to conform to that image, seeking validation. But God's verses only point to manifest truth. Consequently, these people ended up worshipping mental idols they set up in their minds, rather than the true God. The author supports this with Quranic verse 3:7, which describes those with deviation in their hearts who follow ambiguous verses seeking discord and misinterpretation.

Key Terms
المعطلة
المجسمة
ظواهر النصوص
محكم
متشابه
مجاز
استعارة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Anthropomorphists are simply following the literal meaning of the Quran.
Correction: In fact, they selectively choose ambiguous texts, ignore clear texts and linguistic devices (metaphor, trope), and impose their own imagination onto the Quran.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the root error of the anthropomorphists (al-mujassima)?
A) They deny all of God's attributes.
B) They imagine God in a human form based on their own fantasies and then seek Quranic support.
C) They reject the Quran entirely.
D) They only follow the clear verses (muhkam).

Key Takeaway
The anthropomorphists' error is not literalism but projecting their imagination onto the Quran while ignoring its clear verses and figurative language, ultimately worshipping mental idols.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself clinging to a verse of the Quran because it seemed to support a comfortable image of God you already held, while ignoring other verses that challenged that image? How will you now commit to submitting your understanding to the whole of revelation, not just the parts that fit your desires?
?
The author says the anthropomorphists ended up worshipping 'idols in their heads.' Is there any mental picture of God—perhaps formed by culture, upbringing, or personal preference—that you have not tested against the clear teachings of the Quran and Sunnah? What would it cost you to abandon that image and seek only the truth?
?
Quran 3:7 warns of those with deviation in their hearts who follow the ambiguous verses seeking discord. Look honestly at your own heart: is there any desire for novelty, controversy, or self-validation that makes you prefer ambiguous interpretations over the clear, straightforward ones? What concrete step will you take today to purify your intention in reading the Quran?

Refutation of Mu'tazilite Inherent Good and Evil
Buti outlines and criticizes the Mu'tazilite doctrine of inherent good and evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite position on rational good and evil and Buti's critique of its internal inconsistency.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazilites contradicted themselves by claiming inherent good and evil while denying external compulsion on God.

Buti now engages with a major theological opponent—the Mu'tazila. They claimed good and evil are inherent in things and that God must do what is best. Buti shows how their reasoning leads to the brink of disbelief and ultimately collapses into self-contradiction. Let's see his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
Notice how Buti moves from stating their view to harsh criticism.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite claims
List the three key claims: inherent good/evil, God must do the best, and reason alone is sufficient.
These are the foundations of their doctrine.
3
See Buti's severe critique
Buti says they stand on the brink of disbelief and that their inconsistency is nowhere more apparent.
This is a strong condemnation.
4
Spot the contradiction
Notice that they say 'must from Him' not 'upon Him', but this contradicts their initial claim that good and evil are inherent in things.
The tension between external vs internal compulsion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خلاف المعتزلة في هذه المسألة واعلم أن المعتزلة خالفوا أهل السنة والجماعة في هذه المسألة ، فاعتبروا أن للأشياء حسناً وقبحاً عقليين منبعثين من ذات الشيء ، وقرروا بموجب ذلك أن أحكام الله تعالى لابد أن تسير وفق الأصلح والأحسن ، وأن ذلك واجب من الله عز وجل ، وأن العقل وحده يحكم في الأشياء ويعرف حكم الله فيها ، ولذلك فالعقلاء كلهم مكلفون ، سواء بعثت إليهم الرسل أم لا ، والرسول في الآية هو العقل ، فيما زعموا · ولقد زل المعتزلة في هذه المسألة زلات كثيرة ، ولم يظهر تهافت أفكارهم في مسألة كما ظهر في هذه المسألة . ولقد علموا أنهم في كلامهم هذا يقفون على شفير الكفر ، وليس بينهم وبينه إلا أن يقولوا : إن مصالح الكون هي الحاكم على شرع الله وأفعاله ، وهو نتيجة طبيعية لتصورهم وحكمهم على الأشياء بالحسن والقبح الذاتيين . إلا أنهم لم يقولوا إنه يجب على الله الأصلح ، ولكنهم قالوا : يجب منه الأصلح ، فهم لا يعنون بالوجوب إجباراً خارجياً له ، وإنما يقصدون أن صفة الكمال في الله هي منبع هذا الوجوب . وهذا كلام حسن ، ولكنه مضطرب مع أصلهم الأول الذي اعتبروه وهو ثبوت صفة الحسن والقبح في ذات الأشياء ابتداء .
The disagreement of the Mu'tazila on this issue. Know that the Mu'tazila disagreed with Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah on this issue. They considered that things have rational good and evil emanating from the essence of the thing, and they decided accordingly that the rulings of God Almighty must proceed according to what is most beneficial and best, and that is obligatory on the part of God Almighty, and that the intellect alone judges in things and knows God's ruling in them. Therefore, all rational beings are obligated, whether messengers are sent to them or not, and 'the messenger' in the verse is the intellect, according to their claim. And indeed, the Mu'tazila have committed many errors in this issue, and the inconsistency of their ideas has not appeared in any issue as it has appeared in this issue. They knew that in this speech of theirs they stand on the brink of disbelief, and between them and it there is only that they say: 'The interests of the universe are the ruler over God's law and His actions,' and that is a natural result of their conception and judgment of things by inherent good and evil. However, they did not say that the most beneficial is obligatory upon God, but they said: 'The most beneficial is obligatory from Him.' They do not mean by obligation an external compulsion upon Him, but they intend that the attribute of perfection in God is the source of this obligation. This is fine speech, but it is inconsistent with their first principle that they considered: the establishment of the attribute of good and evil in the essences of things from the beginning.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position on rational good and evil. Buti begins by stating that the Mu'tazila oppose Ahl al-Sunnah by claiming that things have inherent rational good and evil, and that God's rulings must align with what is most beneficial and best, as an obligation from God. They also claim that reason alone can judge and know God's rulings, making all rational beings obligated even without prophets, interpreting the 'messenger' in the verse as reason. Buti then criticizes them harshly, saying they have made many errors and that their inconsistency is most evident here. They nearly fell into disbelief by implying that cosmic interests govern God's law. However, they avoided that by saying the obligation is from God, not upon God, meaning God's perfection necessitates the best. Buti acknowledges this as fine but notes it contradicts their initial assumption that good and evil are inherent in things from the start.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الأصلح
الحسن والقبح العقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Mu'tazilite position is internally consistent.
Correction: Buti shows that their nuance (obligation from God's perfection) contradicts their foundational claim that good and evil are inherent in things.

Checkpoint
What does Buti identify as the internal contradiction in the Mu'tazilite position?
A) They say God must do the best but then deny that He is compelled externally.
B) They affirm inherent good and evil but also rely on reason alone.
C) They claim the intellect is a messenger but reject prophets.
D) They say the universe's interests govern God's actions but then say God's perfection is the source.

Key Takeaway
Buti exposes that the Mu'tazilite attempt to avoid external compulsion leads to a contradiction with their foundational belief in inherent good and evil.

Are you letting God be God, or are you imposing your own standards on Him through your sense of what is 'wise' or 'fair'? Will you hold onto any resentment against a divine command that seems suboptimal to you?
?
The Mu'tazila stood on the brink of disbelief by elevating the intellect above scripture. Where in your own practice do you unconsciously allow culture, logic, or personal preference to override a clear text? How will you submit that area to Allah's absolute wisdom today?

Refutation of the Mu'tazila on Rational Good and Evil
Buti refutes the Mu'tazila belief in inherent rational goodness and evil of things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila doctrine of rational good and evil and Buti's refutation showing its internal inconsistency.

Core Idea
Inherent good and evil in things leads to a contradiction with God's freedom.

Buti takes on the Mu'tazila claim that actions have inherent goodness or evil discoverable by reason. He argues that this view leads to the dangerous conclusion that God's actions are constrained by an external standard, bringing it close to disbelief. The passage lays out the Mu'tazila position, their attempted escape, and the flaw in their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila claim
Read the first part of the passage carefully to understand what the Mu'tazila believed about good and evil, reason, and obligation.
Notice that they claimed all rational beings are accountable even without prophets.
2
Understand Buti's criticism
Buti points out that the Mu'tazila themselves knew they were close to disbelief. Their claim that 'the interests of the universe judge God's law' is a natural outcome of their premise.
They stood on the brink of disbelief.
3
Examine their attempted escape
The Mu'tazila rephrased 'obligatory upon God' to 'obligatory from God' to avoid external compulsion, but Buti shows this is inconsistent with their original premise of intrinsic good and evil.
This is the key inconsistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خلاف المعتزلة في هذه المسألة
واعلم أن المعتزلة خالفوا أهل السنة والجماعة في هذه المسألة ، فاعتبروا أن للأشياء حسناً وقبحاً عقليين منبعثين من ذات الشيء ، وقرروا بموجب ذلك أن أحكام الله تعالى لابد أن تسير وفق الأصلح والأحسن ، وأن ذلك واجب من الله عز وجل ، وأن العقل وحده يحكم في الأشياء ويعرف حكم الله فيها ، ولذلك فالعقلاء كلهم مكلفون ، سواء بعثت إليهم الرسل أم لا ، والرسول في الآية هو العقل ، فيما زعموا
·
ولقد زل المعتزلة في هذه المسألة زلات كثيرة ، ولم يظهر تهافت أفكارهم في مسألة كما ظهر في هذه المسألة . ولقد علموا أنهم في كلامهم هذا يقفون على شفير الكفر ، وليس بينهم وبينه إلا أن يقولوا : إن مصالح الكون هي الحاكم على شرع الله وأفعاله ، وهو نتيجة طبيعية لتصورهم وحكمهم على الأشياء بالحسن والقبح الذاتيين . إلا أنهم لم يقولوا إنه يجب على الله الأصلح ، ولكنهم قالوا : يجب منه الأصلح ، فهم لا يعنون بالوجوب إجباراً خارجياً له ، وإنما يقصدون أن صفة الكمال في الله هي منبع هذا الوجوب . وهذا كلام حسن ، ولكنه مضطرب مع أصلهم الأول الذي اعتبروه وهو ثبوت صفة الحسن والقبح في ذات الأشياء ابتداء .
·
✩
(1) إذا أردت أن تقف على مزيد من بيان أن صفة الحسن والقبح في الأشياء كلها اعتباري فقط ، فارجع إلى ماكتب في ذلك الإمام الغزالي في المستصفى ، فقد أتى فيه بكلام في منتهى الدقة والروعة ، وستجد فيه نظرية رد الفعل الشرطي التي يتباهى بعض أرباع العلماء بأنها من بدائع العصر الحديث ، فارجع إلى المستصفى ( ج ١ ص ٥٧ ) .
Disagreement of the Mu'tazila in this matter. Know that the Mu'tazila opposed Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a in this matter. They considered that things have rational goodness and evil emanating from the essence of the thing, and they determined accordingly that the rulings of God Almighty must proceed according to the most beneficial and best, and that this is obligatory from God Almighty, and that reason alone judges things and knows God's ruling in them. Therefore, all rational beings are accountable, whether messengers were sent to them or not, and the messenger in the verse is reason, according to their claim. And the Mu'tazila have slipped many slips in this matter, and their incoherence has not appeared in any matter as it appeared in this matter. They knew that in this speech they are standing on the brink of disbelief, and nothing separates them from it except saying: 'The interests of the universe are the judge over God's law and His actions.' And it is a natural result of their conception and their judgment on things by inherent goodness and evil. However, they did not say that what is most beneficial is obligatory upon God, but they said: it is obligatory from Him. They do not mean by obligation an external compulsion upon Him, but rather they intend that the attribute of perfection in God is the source of this obligation. This is good speech, but it is inconsistent with their first principle which they adopted, namely the affirmation of the attribute of goodness and evil in the essence of things ab initio. (Footnote) If you wish to see more explanation that the attribute of goodness and evil in all things is only contingent/imputed, then refer to what Imam al-Ghazali wrote about that in al-Mustasfa, for he brought forth speech of utmost precision and brilliance. You will find in it the theory of conditioned reflex which some scholars boast as being among the innovations of the modern age. So refer to al-Mustasfa (vol. 1, p. 57).
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila position on the rational basis of good and evil. Buti begins by stating the Mu'tazila view: they believed that actions have inherent goodness or evil, discoverable by reason, and that God's rulings must conform to what is most beneficial. They concluded that all rational beings are morally accountable even without prophets, interpreting the 'messenger' as reason. Buti then points out the inconsistency: the Mu'tazila claim they are not imposing obligation on God but deriving it from His perfection, yet their initial premise of inherent good and evil in things contradicts this, because if good and evil are intrinsic, then God must act accordingly, which is a form of external constraint. Buti notes that the Mu'tazila themselves sensed they were close to disbelief. The footnote recommends al-Ghazali's al-Mustasfa for further insight that all attributions of good and evil are imputed (i'tibari), not real.

Key Terms
الحسن والقبح العقليين
الأصلح
الوجوب
الاعتبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila believed they could avoid kufr by saying 'obligatory from God' instead of 'obligatory upon God'.
Correction: Buti shows that this rephrasing is inconsistent with their own premise that good and evil are intrinsic to actions, because if actions are intrinsically good or evil, then God's obligation to choose the good is inherent in the nature of things, not just a consequence of His perfection.

Checkpoint
What did the Mu'tazila claim about the role of reason in determining God's rulings?
A) Reason is subordinate to revelation.
B) Reason alone can know God's rulings and all rational beings are accountable.
C) Reason is only for understanding revelation.
D) Reason is fallible and cannot know good and evil.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila doctrine of intrinsic good and evil leads to a contradiction when they try to avoid external constraint on God, revealing the inconsistency in their system.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you decide something is 'good' or 'bad', do you ever rely solely on your own reasoning without first checking what God has commanded? What is one area of your life where you need to submit your personal judgment to divine revelation today?
?
The Mu'tazila believed that reason alone could suffice for moral accountability. In what ways have you trusted your intellect over scripture when making a moral decision? What step will you take this week to prioritize God's word over your own reasoning?
?
Buti points out that the Mu'tazila's inconsistency nearly led to kufr. Is there a belief you hold that, if you followed it to its logical conclusion, might lead you away from complete submission to God? Will you examine that belief today and align it with orthodox teaching?

The Mu'tazila Argument from 'Lan' for the Impossibility of Seeing Allah
Mu'tazila linguistic argument from 'lan' for perpetual negation of vision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila used the word 'lan' in the Qur'an to argue that seeing Allah is impossible both in this life and the afterlife.

Core Idea
Lan means perpetual negation, extending denial of vision to Hereafter.

The Mu'tazila were known for their rational approach to theology. One of their key proofs against the possibility of seeing Allah involves a subtle linguistic argument about the Arabic word 'lan'. In this passage, the author presents al-Zamakhshari's interpretation of 'lan' as indicating absolute and perpetual negation, thereby excluding any possibility of vision in the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key Qur'anic verse
The argument revolves around the verse 'lan tarāni' (You will not see Me). Recall that this is from the story of Musa (AS) asking to see Allah.
The specific verse is not quoted in the passage but is referenced by the word 'lan'.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila interpretation of 'lan'
Al-Zamakhshari interprets 'lan' as indicating absolute negation, meaning the denial is perpetual and includes both this world and the Hereafter.
This is a unique interpretation among scholars.
3
Consider the implication for vision of Allah
If 'lan' negates forever, then vision is impossible in the Hereafter as well, which directly opposes the Sunni belief that the believers will see Allah in Paradise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مستحيلة. ومن أجل تقوية هذا المعنى وتأكيده، فسر الزمخشري (وهو من المعتزلة) لن بالنفي المؤبد لتتم الدلالة في الآية على أن الرؤية منتفية في الدنيا والآخرة معاً، ولا نظن أحداً غير الزمخشري فسر لن بالنفي المؤبد. كما استدلوا على نفي الرؤية بقوله تعالى: {لا تُدْرِكُهُ الأَبْصَارُ وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الأَبْصَارَ وَهُوَ اللَّطِيفُ الْخَبِيرُ} [الأنعام: 103] قالوا: فقد نفى الله عز وجل أن يدركه أحد بالبصر، والإدراك بالبصر هو الرؤية.
Impossible. And to strengthen this meaning and emphasize it, al-Zamakhshari (who is from the Mu'tazila) interpreted 'lan' as absolute negation so that the indication in the verse is that vision is negated in this world and the hereafter together. And we do not think anyone other than al-Zamakhshari interpreted 'lan' as absolute negation. Likewise, they argued for the negation of vision by His saying, the Most High: {Vision perceives Him not, and He perceives all vision; and He is the Subtle, the Aware} [al-An'am: 103]. They said: Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, has negated that anyone perceives Him by sight, and perception by sight is vision.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage presents the first set of arguments from the Mu'tazila against the possibility of seeing Allah. It begins by mentioning al-Zamakhshari's interpretation of the word 'lan' in the verse 'lan tarāni' as meaning perpetual negation, extending to both this world and the Hereafter. The author notes that this interpretation is unique to al-Zamakhshari. Then the passage presents another proof: the verse 'La tudrikuhu al-abṣār…' which is understood to negate the possibility of perceiving Allah with sight, equating perception with vision. The Mu'tazila conclude from this that vision of Allah is impossible.

Key Terms
لن
النفي المؤبد
الرؤية
الزمخشري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'lan' always means perpetual negation.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that only al-Zamakhshari interpreted 'lan' as absolute negation in this context, indicating that this interpretation is not universally accepted.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how did al-Zamakhshari interpret the word 'lan' in the verse about seeing Allah?
A) As a temporary negation
B) As absolute and perpetual negation
C) As a question
D) As an affirmation

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila used a unique interpretation of 'lan' to argue that seeing Allah is impossible forever.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'lan tarāni', do you feel a sense of loss at the thought of never seeing Allah, or does it strengthen your hope in the Hereafter where the Ahl al-Sunnah believe vision is possible? How does the Mu'tazila interpretation challenge or affirm that hope?
?
The author points out that al-Zamakhshari's interpretation of 'lan' is unique. In your own study of Islam, are you tempted to accept a minority opinion that feels more 'logical' without checking whether it contradicts the consensus of the Salaf? Where in your life might this be happening?
?
If the possibility of seeing Allah were truly impossible forever, as the Mu'tazila argue, would that change the way you long for Jannah? Does your heart yearn for the vision of Allah, and how do you guard that hope against doubts raised by such arguments?

The Mu'tazila Argument from 'La Tudrikuhu al-Absar'
Mu'tazila proof from Qur'an against vision of Allah by equating perception with vision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila used the Qur'anic verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' to prove that Allah cannot be seen.

Core Idea
Perception by sight equals vision, and the verse denies both.

The Mu'tazila also drew upon another Qur'anic verse to support their denial of the vision of Allah. They interpreted the phrase 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' (Vision perceives Him not) as a definitive negation of any possibility of seeing Allah. This lesson examines their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse from Surah al-An'am
The verse is: 'لا تدركه الأبصار وهو يدرك الأبصار' meaning 'Vision perceives Him not, and He perceives all vision.'
This verse is often cited in discussions about the beatific vision.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila interpretation
They equate 'idrak' (perception) with 'ru'ya' (vision), and conclude that the verse negates the possibility of seeing Allah.
This interpretation assumes that 'idrak' and 'ru'ya' are synonymous.
3
Consider the implication
If the verse negates perception by sight, then it negates seeing Allah in both this world and the Hereafter.
This contradicts the Sunni position that believers will see Allah in Paradise.

The New View on Miracles and Its Claims
Buti describes a modernist view that Muhammad's only miracle is the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the content and claims of a modernist view that restricts Prophet Muhammad's miracles to the Qur'an alone.

Core Idea
A modern trend claims the Qur'an is Muhammad's sole miracle.

This lesson introduces a controversial modern viewpoint regarding the miracles of Prophet Muhammad. The passage outlines the claim that the Prophet's only miracle is the Qur'an, dismissing other miracles attributed to previous prophets. Understanding this view is important for engaging with contemporary discussions on Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's description come through.
Notice that Buti presents this as a 'new view'.
2
Identify the core claim
The passage states that the Prophet's only miracle is the Qur'an. Find the exact phrase that expresses this.
The phrase is 'لم تسجل له سوى معجزة واحدة هي القرآن'.
3
Examine the supporting arguments
Note how followers of this view support their claim: they deny other miracles, cite Quran 6:109, and argue that the Prophet addressed people within their understanding.
4
Recognize the broader context
Buti mentions that this view is now found in many modern books and is associated with the slogan of 'religious reform'. Consider why this might be significant.
The term 'religious reform' is key (الإصلاح الديني).
5
Reflect on the implications
Think about how this view differs from traditional Islamic beliefs about miracles. What does it imply about the role of miracles in proving prophethood?
This connects to broader discussions in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رأي جديد في بحث المعجزات وبيان ما ينبغي أن يكون عليه موقف المسلمين منها ، لا سيما معجزات سيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم . وخلاصة هذا الاتجاه تتمثل في اعتماد أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم تسجل له سوى معجزة واحدة هي القرآن ، فمعجزته الوحيدة التي أكرمه الله بها هي هذا القرآن الذي تنزل عليه . أما الخوارق الأخرى التي ظهرت على أيدي الأنبياء السابقين مما يدركه ويفهمه العقل فقد كان منكراً لها غير عابئ بها ولا ملتفت إلى المطالبين بها ، ويرددون أنه كان يؤكد دائماً بأن المعجزات والخوارق ليست من شأنه وليس له إليها من سبيل ويكثرون في هذا من الاستشهاد بقوله تعالى : ﴿ قُل إنما الآياتُ عِندَ اللهِ ﴾ [الأنعام : ۱۰۹] ويزعمون أن هذا من الخصائص العليـا لـه عليه الصلاة والسلام فهو لم يخاطب الناس بما لا يفهمون ، ولم يعاملهم بما وراء حدود العلم الذي يدركه البشر . وإنك لتقرأ هذا الكلام وتجد هذا الاتجاه في كثير من الكتب الحديثة اليوم ، بعد أن تبناه من قبل أفراد معدودون تبنوا الدعوة إليه والتبشير به وارتبطت أسماؤهم من أجل ذلك بشعار ( الإصلاح الديني ( الذي شاع لأسباب معينة منذ ذلك اليوم .
A new view regarding the study of miracles and an explanation of what the attitude of Muslims towards them should be, especially the miracles of our master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. The summary of this trend is represented in the adoption that the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, had only one miracle recorded for him, which is the Qur'an; his sole miracle with which God honored him is this Qur'an that was revealed to him. As for the other marvels that appeared at the hands of previous prophets, which the intellect perceives and understands, they were deniers of them, not caring about them nor paying attention to those who demanded them, and they repeat that he always emphasized that miracles and marvels are not his concern and he has no way to them, and they frequently cite in this His saying, the Exalted: {Say, 'The signs are only with God'} [Al-An'am: 109], and they claim that this is among the supreme characteristics of him, peace and blessings be upon him, because he did not address people with what they do not understand, nor did he treat them with what lies beyond the boundaries of knowledge that humans perceive. And you read this statement and find this trend in many modern books today, after it was previously adopted by a few individuals who undertook the call to it and preaching it, and their names became associated with that under the slogan of 'religious reform' which spread for certain reasons since that day.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage describes a modern trend regarding miracles. Buti first states the topic: a new opinion on miracles and the correct Muslim stance, especially concerning the miracles of Prophet Muhammad. He then summarizes the trend: it holds that the Prophet's only miracle is the Qur'an. Other extraordinary events from previous prophets are denied or dismissed. Followers of this view claim the Prophet always insisted that miracles are not his concern, citing Qur'an 6:109. They consider this a supreme trait because he addressed people within their understanding. Buti notes that this view is now found in many modern books, adopted by a few individuals who promoted it under the banner of 'religious reform'.

?

Colonial Origins of the Anti-Miracle Trend
Buti traces the trend's origin to British colonialism and its aims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's claim that the anti-miracle trend originated from British colonial policy rather than from natural intellectual development.

Core Idea
The anti-miracle trend was a colonial tool, not a natural product of Islamic thought.

This lesson examines Buti's historical analysis of the anti-miracle trend. He argues that its roots lie not in scholarly debate but in British colonial strategy following the occupation of Egypt. We will see how he connects the trend's emergence to a deliberate intellectual intervention designed to weaken Muslim religious attachment.

Guided Path
1
Read Buti's historical claim
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note how Buti frames the origin as deliberate and tied to the British occupation of Egypt.
He mentions 'intended distant causes' to indicate premeditation.
2
Identify the colonial context
Recognize that Buti specifies British knowledge that military force alone was insufficient for stability, especially after the caliphate's fall.
3
Find the stated goal
Locate the phrase describing the intellectual methodology's aim: to change Muslim thinking and distance them from religious intensity, aligning them with European thought.
The goal is political, not theological.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this refutes the idea that the trend emerged naturally from within Islamic thought. Buti presents it as an externally imposed project.
This is a key historiographical argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونحن نبدأ فنحدثك عن مبدأ هذا الاتجاه وأسبابه المقصودة البعيدة ثم نناقشه كما قلنا تحت مجهر العلم والعقل ونعرضه لدلائل التاريخ نفسه . إن مولد هذا الاتجاه في عالمنا الإسلامي يعود إلى تاريخ الاحتلال البريطاني لمصر . فقد احتلت بريطانيا يومئذ مصر وهي تعلم أن اعتمادها على القوة العسكرية وحدها لن يفيدها الاستقرار، ولن يمكن لها موطئ قدمها في البلدة التي احتلتها ، خصوصاً وإن العالم الإسلامي قريب العهد بانهيار الخلافة الإسلامية . فرأت - كما هو شأنها دائماً ـ أن لا بد من الاستعانة بمنهج فكري يغير من تفكير المسلمين تغييراً يقصيهم عن هذه الشدة في التمسك بالدين والتضحية من أجله والاعتماد عليه وحده . ويجعلهم يلتقون مع الفكر الأوربي في أوسع قدر ممكن من سبل الحياة .
And we begin to tell you about the origin of this trend and its intended distant causes, then we will discuss it, as we said, under the microscope of science and reason, and present it to the proofs of history itself. The birth of this trend in our Islamic world goes back to the history of the British occupation of Egypt. Britain occupied Egypt at that time knowing that relying on military force alone would not avail it stability, nor would it enable it to plant its foothold in the country it had occupied, especially since the Islamic world was recently acquainted with the collapse of the Islamic caliphate. So it saw - as is always its custom - that it must resort to an intellectual methodology that would change the thinking of Muslims in a way that distances them from this intensity in clinging to religion and sacrificing for it and relying on it alone, and makes them meet European thought in the widest possible scope of the ways of life.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage transitions from describing the trend to investigating its origins. Buti announces he will discuss the trend's principle and distant causes, then examine it with science and history. He asserts that the birth of this trend in the Islamic world goes back to the British occupation of Egypt. Britain knew military power alone wouldn't ensure stability, especially since the caliphate had recently fallen. So they adopted a policy: use an intellectual methodology to change Muslim thinking, reducing their intense attachment to religion and sacrifice for it, and aligning them with European thought. This is the underlying motive.

Key Terms
الاحتلال البريطاني
منهج فكري
الإصلاح الاجتماعي والديني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the anti-miracle trend emerged naturally from within Islamic intellectual circles.
Correction: Buti argues it was deliberately introduced by British colonialism to weaken Muslim religious commitment.

Checkpoint

D) To revive the caliphate

Key Takeaway
The anti-miracle trend was a colonial strategy, not a natural development in Islamic thought.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If a major trend in Islamic thought was deliberately engineered by a colonial power to weaken your faith, what does that reveal about other ideas you accept today? Are you willing to trace the origins of your own beliefs, even if it disturbs you?
?
Buti says the British wanted to distance Muslims from 'this intensity in clinging to religion and sacrificing for it.' How intense is your own attachment to your religion? Have you already been influenced by trends that soften that attachment without you realizing it?
?
This lesson strips away the comfort of thinking that all intellectual movements are innocent. It demands you become a detective of your own Aqeedah. Will you commit to examining every belief you hold with the same critical eye Buti uses here, starting today?

Britain's Target: Al-Azhar
Buti explains the British reform plan targeting Al-Azhar and cites Lord Lloyd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Britain targeted Al-Azhar as the first field of its social and religious reform, and how Buti supports this with historical evidence from Lord Lloyd's memoirs.

Core Idea
Al-Azhar was the key to controlling Islamic leadership—both intellectually and spiritually.

This passage reveals the colonial strategy behind the so-called 'reform' of Al-Azhar. Buti shows that Britain understood Al-Azhar's central role in leading Egypt and the wider Islamic world, so any reform had to start there. He then presents a firsthand testimony from the British High Commissioner to confirm this plan.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage slowly, then follow with the literal translation. Get a sense of Buti's argument and the quote from Lord Lloyd.
Pay attention to the shift from Buti's own analysis to the quoted testimony.
2
Identify Buti's main claim
Buti states that Britain implemented 'social and religious reform' starting with Al-Azhar because Al-Azhar held leadership of Egypt and beyond. Locate the sentence that emphasizes Al-Azhar's role in every national, religious, intellectual, and social issue.
Key phrase: 'لم تكن هناك من قضية وطنية أو دينية أو مشكلة فكرية أو اجتماعية إلا والأزهر هو الرأس المدبر'
3
Understand the methodological statement
Buti pauses to clarify that he does not rely on Western conjectural methods but on sound scientific methodology. Why does he insert this here? Reflect on the importance of trustworthy sources in historical analysis.
This is a recurring theme in Buti's work—defending traditional Islamic methodology.
4
Examine Lord Lloyd's testimony
Read the quote from Lord Lloyd's memoirs. What does he say about Al-Azhar's education and its students? How does this support Buti's argument that Britain viewed Al-Azhar as an obstacle?
Note the phrase 'غرور التعصب الديني' (arrogance of religious fanaticism) and 'خطوة جلية الخطر' (clearly dangerous step).
5
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Consider the bigger picture: Al-Azhar's role as a bastion of Islamic knowledge made it a target. How might this historical insight inform our understanding of contemporary challenges?

وقامت بريطانيا بهذا الدافع ، بتطبيق ما أطلقت عليه اسم الإصلاح الاجتماعي والديني : وكان الميدان الأول لهذا ( الإصلاح ) هو الجامع الأزهر المتمثل في مناهجه الدرسية وطريقته الفكرية . ذلك أن قيادة القطر المصري كله كانت إذ ذاك بید الأزهر ، وكان إشعاعه يتجاوزه إلى كثير من البقاع الإسلامية الأخرى ، فلم تكن هناك من قضية وطنية أو دينية أو مشكلة فكرية أو اجتماعية إلا والأزهر هو الرأس المدبر والمفكر فيها وهو المحرك لها ، لذلك فلم يكن لينجح أي ) إصلاح ( ديني أو فكري من وجهة نظر بريطانيا إلا إذا بدأ بالأزهر . وينبغي أن نذكرك هنا بأننا لا نتبع فيا نرويه من أحداث ووقائع تاريخية ، منهج الاسترداد أو التوسم الذي يتعلق به دون غيره منهجيـو الغرب خصوصاً بالنسبة لتاريخنا وإسلامنا ، ولكننا نتبع المنهج العلمي السليم الذي أوضحناه والتزمناه . ولعلك تتساءل ، فمن أين علمنا أن بريطانيا وضعت لنفسها هذا المخطط ، وضاقت ذرعاً بالإسلام وبأزهره ؟! فاسمع ما يقوله في ذلك اللورد لويد ، المندوب السامي لمصر إذ ذاك ، في مذكراته التي سماها ( Egypt Since Cromer : مصر منذ أيام كرومر ) . يقول : ( إن التعليم الوطني عندما قدم الإنكليز ، كان في قبضة الجامعة الأزهرية الشديدة التمسك بالدين والتي كانت أساليبها الجافة تقف حاجزاً في طريق أي إصلاح تعليمي ، وكان الطلبة الذين يتخرجون من هذه الجامعة قدراً عظيماً من غرور التعصب الديني ، ( تنبـه جـيـداً إلى معنى يحملون معهم الكلام ) فلو أمكن تطوير الأزهر لكانت خطوة جلية الخطر . فليس من اليسير هذا .
And Britain, with this motive, implemented what it called social and religious reform: and the first field for this 'reform' was the Al-Azhar Mosque, represented in its curricula and intellectual methodology. That is because the leadership of all of Egypt was at that time in the hands of Al-Azhar, and its radiation extended to many other Islamic lands; there was no national or religious issue or intellectual or social problem except that Al-Azhar was the directing head, the thinker in it, and the mover of it. Therefore, no religious or intellectual 'reform' from Britain's point of view could succeed unless it began with Al-Azhar. And we should remind you here that we do not follow in what we narrate of historical events and facts the method of retrieval or conjecture which the Western methodologists adhere to especially regarding our history and Islam, but we follow the sound scientific methodology which we have explained and committed to. And perhaps you ask: from where did we know that Britain set this plan for itself and became impatient with Islam and its Azhar? So listen to what Lord Lloyd, the High Commissioner for Egypt at that time, says in his memoirs which he called 'Egypt Since Cromer'. He says: 'National education when the English arrived was in the grip of the Al-Azhar University, extremely attached to religion, whose dry methods stood as a barrier in the way of any educational reform, and the students who graduated from this university carried a great amount of the arrogance of religious fanaticism. (Pay close attention to the meaning they carry with the speech.) So if it were possible to develop Al-Azhar, it would be a clearly dangerous step. This is not easy.'
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage details Britain's implementation of its reform plan, focusing on Al-Azhar. Buti explains that Britain applied 'social and religious reform' first to Al-Azhar because it was the intellectual leader of Egypt and the Islamic world. Without reforming Al-Azhar, no reform would succeed. Then Buti asserts his methodology: he does not rely on Western methods of conjecture but on sound scientific method. He then cites Lord Lloyd's memoirs as evidence. Lloyd states that national education was in Al-Azhar's grip, students were fanatical, and reforming Al-Azhar would be a dangerous step. This confirms British awareness of Al-Azhar's influence and their desire to change it.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Al-Azhar's resistance to reform was due to stubbornness or backwardness.
Correction: Buti shows that Al-Azhar was deliberately targeted by colonial powers because it was a powerful Islamic institution; the resistance was a defense of Islamic identity.

Buti uses a primary source—Lord Lloyd's memoirs—to demonstrate that Britain's reform plan deliberately targeted Al-Azhar because of its leadership role in the Islamic world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Buti relies on a primary source from the colonizer himself to expose the truth. How many of your beliefs about history or current events are based on secondhand or biased accounts? What is one historical claim you can verify with an original source this week?
?
Al-Azhar stood as a barrier to colonial plans because it held real leadership and influence. In your own life, where have you allowed external pressures to weaken your commitment to Islamic principles under the guise of 'progress'? What will you do today to strengthen that barrier?

Formation of a New School and British Gain
Buti concludes that a new school formed and Britain weakened the religious deterrent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti ties the emergence of a new intellectual school at Al-Azhar to British colonial goals and the weakening of the religious deterrent.

Core Idea
A new school's philosophy became a tool for weakening religious deterrent under British occupation.

In this concluding passage, Buti summarizes the outcome of the intellectual direction he has been discussing. He declares that a new school formed and spread its philosophy from Al-Azhar's pulpit. Then he asks a rhetorical question about what Britain gained, and the answer is the weakening of the religious deterrent in people's souls. This passage directly links the intellectual movement to British colonial interests.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the English translation. Pay attention to the rhetorical question and the answer.
The passage ends mid-sentence in the OCR; the full meaning is clear from the context.
2
Identify the two main claims
First, the formation of a new intellectual school spreading from Al-Azhar. Second, the answer to what Britain gained: weakening of the religious deterrent.
Notice how the author connects these two claims.
3
Reflect on the link between thought and power
Ask yourself: Why would weakening the religious deterrent benefit a colonial power? How does the author characterize the intellectual movement?
This step connects the passage to broader themes of religion and colonialism.

Commentary
This concluding passage states that a new intellectual school (madrasa fikriyya jadida) was formed from this direction and spread its philosophy from Al-Azhar's pulpit, with expected impact under the 'ominous occupation' (al-ihtilal al-mash'um). The author poses a rhetorical question: what did Britain gain? The answer: the weakening of the religious deterrent (al-wazi‘ al-dini) in people's souls. The passage directly links the intellectual movement to British colonial interests.

The Misappropriation of 'Science' to Deny Miracles
Buti describes reformist misuse of 'science' to reject miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how reformist thinkers misused the term 'science' as a pretext to reject miracles and the supernatural, and why Buti considers this a distorted understanding of science.

Core Idea
Science does not require denying miracles; reformists used 'science' as soap to wash away the supernatural.

Buti begins his critique by describing how the British exploited the reformists' infatuation with Western science, convincing them that true science demands rejection of miracles. He then expresses pity for their contradictory ideas, which are filled with the word 'science' but devoid of its substance. This passage lays the groundwork for his attack on the reformist school.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening critique
Read the Arabic passage where Buti describes how the English used 'science' to convince reformists to deny miracles. Notice the metaphor of 'soap'.
Buti uses strong language: 'soap to wash their minds and researches'.
2
Identify the reformist error
Buti says their books are full of 'science' but stripped of its shadows. What does he mean by 'shadows'?
He means the true essence or substance of science.
3
Reflect on the metaphor
Consider why Buti uses the image of soap. What does it imply about the reformists' use of science?
It suggests a cleansing that removes all traces of the supernatural, which Buti sees as misguided.

ولقد رأينا كيف وقع اختيار الإذاعة الإسرائيلية في رمضان هذا العام) على هذا الكتاب دون غيره ، لتذيع منه فقرات من السيرة النبوية ، أفكان ذلك
(۱) كان ذلك في رمضان عام ١٩٦٨
لأن الإذاعة الإسرائيلية تحرص كل الحرص على أن لا تذيع شيئاً من حياة محمد وسيرته إلا على أسس علمية مجردة ؟!..
وحسبك يقيناً بالقيمة العلمية الرفيعة في كتاب يحلل حياة رسول الله ، أن يكون هو الكتاب الذي يقع عليه اختيار اليهود ليستفاد منه في تغطية برامج دينية للمسلمين في إذاعتها الموجهة !..

وأخذنا ننظر ، وإذا الواقع يسخر من نبوءة محمد فريد وجدي حينما قال وهو يعاني من إحدى غيبوباته العاطفية مع كلمة ( العلم ) : « إن الشرق الإسلامي لما رأى دينه ماثلاً في عالم الأساطير التي قذفـت فيـه الأديان جملة بيد العلم الحديث الغربي ، لم ينبس بكلمة لأنه رأى الأمر أكبر من أن يحاوله ، ولكنه استبطن الإلحاد وتمسك به متيقناً أنه مصير إخوانه كافة متى وصلوا إلى درجته العلمية ((

At a time when they do not possess any useful amount of its meaning, and it happened that the English exploited this state in them and made them understand that (science) is not attained except by denying miracles and the unseen, so they took the word (science) as soap with which to wash their minds and their researches from everything named a miracle or a supernatural event. And any scholar today would pity their confused self-contradictory ideas when he reads them in their books filled with words of (science) and stripped even of its shadows. You read the introduction to the book (The Life of Muhammad) by al-Husayn Haykal, and you see him repeating in pride and self-praise: 'I did not take what the books of biography and hadith have recorded because I preferred to conduct this research on the scientific method...' Rather, you see him reassuring you that he did not take even what is established in al-Bukhari and Muslim, for the sake of the dignity of science!! So what kind of person is this who does not pity the mentality of a researcher who considers what al-Bukhari narrated as a deviation from wonderful strange constraints of scientific caution that are the path of science, while he sees in following the method of the Westerners in inference, intuition, and the approach of guesswork as preserving its dignity and adhering to its methodology and path?!.. And if the method of the Westerners in studying the life of Muhammad is not the scientific method that leads to truth as Husayn Haykal sees, nor the method that our Muslim predecessors followed, then the matter should end in one of two conclusions: either the Westerners believe in the prophethood of Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him) if Husayn Haykal sees that it is truth, or he himself denies his prophethood if he does not see it as truth. And we have seen how the choice of the Israeli radio station in Ramadan of this year fell upon this book specifically, to broadcast from it passages of the prophetic biography. Was that because the Israeli radio station is extremely keen not to broadcast anything from the life of Muhammad and his biography except on purely scientific foundations?!.. And suffice you as certainty of the high scientific value of a book that analyzes the life of the Messenger of God, that it is the book that the Jews choose to benefit from in covering religious programs for Muslims in their directed broadcast!.. Any intellectual knows that that (reformist) school was only established on one pillar, namely infatuation with the word (science) and lacking its content. And here we see today how science itself is taking on the task of sweeping away this (reformist) school through reason and research, and how the vision between science and miracle has become clearer than it was before. The period of infatuation has ended, and the eye has returned to look at the light with all its energy. And we began to look, and behold, reality mocks the prophecy of Muhammad Farid Wajdi when he said, while suffering from one of his emotional swoons with the word (science): 'The Islamic East, when it saw its religion embodied in the world of myths that religions had thrown into it wholesale at the hands of modern Western science, did not utter a word because it saw the matter as too great to attempt, but it internalized atheism and clung to it, convinced that it is the fate of all its brothers when they reach its scientific level.' (1) From an article published by Farid Wajdi in al-Ahram on 30-8-1937 in response to an article written by the scholar Mustafa Sabri, and see the story of the two articles in the book Mawqif al-Aql wa al-Ilm: 4-407. And he had not yet been appointed editor-in-chief of the journal al-Azhar known as (Nur al-Islam). But his ideas qualified him for this position later, succeeding the great scholar al-Allama al-`Azim al-Tabah [؟] Muhammad al-Khidr Husayn, as part of the reformist achievements that the British occupation had planned for the Azhar University specifically and Egyptian society in general (see p. 223 of this book). And no doubt he concealed these ideas after he became editor-in-chief of the great Islamic journal speaking in the name of al-Azhar, and kept them under his tongue for a period.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a sustained polemical critique by Buti against certain reformist Muslim thinkers who uncritically adopted Western scientific methodology and used the word 'science' as a pretext to reject miracles and the supernatural. Buti begins by describing how the British exploited this tendency, convincing people that 'science' requires denying miracles. He then expresses pity for the contradictory ideas in their books, which are full of 'science' but devoid of its true meaning. He specifically attacks Husayn Haykal's book 'Hayat Muhammad', noting that Haykal claims to follow the 'scientific method' by rejecting even authentic hadith from Bukhari and Muslim for the sake of science. Buti finds this absurd: Haykal considers reliance on Bukhari a deviation from scientific caution, yet he follows Western guesswork and inference. Buti then presents a logical dilemma: if the Western method is truly scientific and leads to truth, then it should compel Westerners to accept Muhammad's prophethood; if not, then Haykal himself should deny the prophethood. Buti further highlights that an Israeli radio station chose Haykal's book for Ramadan broadcasts, sarcastically asking if this is because it reflects 'scientific' foundations. He argues that this proves the book's worthlessness from a Muslim perspective. Buti then identifies the root of the reformist school: infatuation with the word 'science' without its substance. He claims that now, true science itself is sweeping away that school, and the relationship between science and miracles is clearer. He concludes by mocking Muhammad Farid Wajdi's prophecy that the Islamic East would embrace atheism upon reaching Western scientific levels. Buti includes a lengthy footnote about Farid Wajdi's later concealment of these ideas after becoming editor of an Azhar journal, implying hypocrisy. Throughout, Buti maintains that genuine science does not contradict Islam or miracles; the problem is a superficial and self-contradictory understanding of 'science'.

Key Terms
العلم (science)
المعجزات (miracles)
المدرسة الإصلاحية (reformist school)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That scientific methodology necessitates denying miracles.
Correction: Buti argues that true science does not require rejecting miracles; the reformists have a superficial and distorted view of science.

Checkpoint
What did the British convince the reformists about science?
A) That science is only for materialists.
B) That attaining science requires denying miracles and the unseen.
C) That science must be based on Western methods.
D) That science should replace religion.

Key Takeaway
The reformists' infatuation with the word 'science' led them to reject miracles without understanding true scientific principles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used terms like 'rational' or 'scientific' to dismiss something from your faith without truly understanding those terms? What did you wash away in that moment, and what was the cost?
?
This passage reveals how the reformists were unknowingly influenced by colonial exploitation. Are there modern influences—media, academia, or social circles—that subtly shape your views on religious matters like miracles? What 'soap' might you be using without realizing it?
?
Buti says scholars pity the reformists' contradictory ideas. Are there contradictions in your own understanding of Islam—areas where you hold positions that conflict because you have borrowed terms or ideas without grasping their full meaning? Will you examine one such contradiction today and seek clarity?

The Contradiction of Husayn Haykal's 'Scientific Method'
Buti criticizes Haykal's rejection of authentic hadith and presents a logical dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's critique of Husayn Haykal's rejection of authentic hadith in the name of science, and the logical dilemma this creates regarding prophethood.

Core Idea
Haykal's 'scientific method' leads to absurd outcomes that undermine his own position on prophethood.

Buti now turns his attention to Husayn Haykal's book 'Hayat Muhammad'. He highlights Haykal's claim to follow the scientific method by discarding even the most authentic hadith from Bukhari and Muslim. Buti finds this self-contradictory and presents a logical dilemma: if the Western method truly leads to truth, it should confirm prophethood; if not, Haykal should deny it outright.

Guided Path
1
Read the critique of Haykal
Read the Arabic passage where Buti quotes Haykal and presents the dilemma. Note the sarcastic tone.
Buti uses exclamation marks to show disbelief.
2
Understand the logical dilemma
Buti says the matter must end in one of two conclusions. What are they?
Either the Westerners accept prophethood, or Haykal must reject it.
3
Reflect on the absurdity
Why does Buti consider it absurd that Haykal rejects Bukhari and Muslim? What does this say about Haykal's understanding of science?
Buti sees reliance on authentic hadith as a sign of scientific caution, not deviation.

الوقت الذي لا يملكون أي قدر مفيد من معناها ، وصادف أن استغل الإنكليز فيهم هذه الحالة فأفهمهم أن ( العلم ( لا يُرقى إليه إلا بإنكار المعجزات والمغيبات ، فاتخذوا من كلمة ( العلم ( صابوناً يغسلون به أدمغتهم وأبحاثهم من كل شيء اسمه معجزة أو خارقة
وإنَّ أي عالم ، ليشفق اليوم على أفكارهم المتهافتة المتناقضة ، عندما يقرؤها في كتبهم المملوءة بكلمات ) العلم ( والمجردة حتى من ظلاله . تقرأ مقدمة كتاب ( حياة محمد ( الحسين هيكل ، وتراه وهو يقول مكرراً في اعتزاز وتنويه بنفسه : ( إنني لم أخذ بما سجلته كتب السيرة والحديث لأنني فضلت أن أجري في هذا البحث على الطريقة العلمية ... ) بل تراه يطمئنك إلى أنه لم يأخذ حتى بما يثبت في البخاري ومسلم ، حفظاً لكرامة العلم ..!!
فأي إنسان هذا الذي لا يشفق على عقلية باحث يرى فيما يرويه البخاري محل اعتزاز وفخر ، انحرافاً عن ضمن قيود رائعة عجيبة من الحيطة العلمية التي هي . جادة العلم : على حين يرى في اتباع طريق الغربيين في الاستنتاج والحدس ونهج التوسم حفظاً لكرامته والتزاماً بمنهجه وجادته ؟!..
وإذا كانت طريقة الغربيين في دراسة حياة محمد ولا هي الطريقة العلمية الموصلة إلى الحق كما يرى حسين هيكل لا الطريقة التي اتبعها أسلافنا المسلمون فإن الأمر ينبغي أن ينتهي إلى إحدى نتيجتين : إما أن يؤمن الغربيون بنبوة محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام إن كان يرى حسين هيكل أنها من الحق ، وإما أن ينكر هو نبوته إن كان لا يرى أنها من الحق
ولقد رأينا كيف وقع اختيار الإذاعة الإسرائيلية في رمضان هذا العام) على هذا الكتاب دون غيره ، لتذيع منه فقرات من السيرة النبوية ، أفكان ذلك
(۱) كان ذلك في رمضان عام ١٩٦٨
لأن الإذاعة الإسرائيلية تحرص كل الحرص على أن لا تذيع شيئاً من حياة محمد وسيرته إلا على أسس علمية مجردة ؟!..
وحسبك يقيناً بالقيمة العلمية الرفيعة في كتاب يحلل حياة رسول الله ، أن يكون هو الكتاب الذي يقع عليه اختيار اليهود ليستفاد منه في تغطية برامج دينية للمسلمين في إذاعتها الموجهة !..
إن أي مفكر ، يعلم بأن تلك المدرسة ( الإصلاحية ) لم تقم إلا على دعـامـة واحدة ، ألا وهي الافتنان بكلمة ( العلم ) والافتقار إلى مضمونها .
وها نحن نرى اليوم كيف أن العلم نفسه هو الذي يتولى كنس هذه المدرسة ) الإصلاحية ( عن طريق العقل والبحث وكيف عادت الرؤية بين العلم والمعجزة أصفى مما كانت عليه من قبل ، فقد انتهت فترة الانبهار وعادت العين تنظر إلى الضوء بكل ما لديها من طاقة
وأخذنا ننظر ، وإذا الواقع يسخر من نبوءة محمد فريد وجدي حينما قال وهو يعاني من إحدى غيبوباته العاطفية مع كلمة ( العلم ) : « إن الشرق الإسلامي لما رأى دينه ماثلاً في عالم الأساطير التي قذفـت فيـه الأديان جملة بيد العلم الحديث الغربي ، لم ينبس بكلمة لأنه رأى الأمر أكبر من أن يحاوله ، ولكنه استبطن الإلحاد وتمسك به متيقناً أنه مصير إخوانه كافة متى وصلوا إلى درجته العلمية ((
(۱) من مقال نشره فريد وجدي في الأهرام في ۳۰ - ۸ - ۱۹۳۷ رداً على مقال كتبه العلامة مصطفى صبري ، وانظر قصة المقالين في كتاب موقف العقل والعلم : ٤ - ٤٠٧ ولم يكن قد نصب فريد وجدي يومها رئيساً لتحرير مجلة الأرهر المعروفة باسم ( نور الإسلام ) . ولكن أفكاره هذه رشحته لتولي هذا المنصب فيما بعد خلفاً للعلامة العظيم التبح محمد الخصر حسين ، كحرء من المنجزات الإصلاحية التي كان قد حطط لها الاحتلال البريطاني بالسبة للجامعة الأزهريه حاصة والمجتمع المصري عامة ( انظر ص ۲۲۳ من هذا الكتاب ) ، ولا جرم أنه طوى أفكاره هذه بعـد أصبح رئيساً لتحرير المجلة الإسلامية الكبرى الناطقة باسم الأزهر ، واحتفظ بها تحت لسـانـه فترة
At a time when they do not possess any useful amount of its meaning, and it happened that the English exploited this state in them and made them understand that (science) is not attained except by denying miracles and the unseen, so they took the word (science) as soap with which to wash their minds and their researches from everything named a miracle or a supernatural event. And any scholar today would pity their confused self-contradictory ideas when he reads them in their books filled with words of (science) and stripped even of its shadows. You read the introduction to the book (The Life of Muhammad) by al-Husayn Haykal, and you see him repeating in pride and self-praise: 'I did not take what the books of biography and hadith have recorded because I preferred to conduct this research on the scientific method...' Rather, you see him reassuring you that he did not take even what is established in al-Bukhari and Muslim, for the sake of the dignity of science!! So what kind of person is this who does not pity the mentality of a researcher who considers what al-Bukhari narrated as a deviation from wonderful strange constraints of scientific caution that are the path of science, while he sees in following the method of the Westerners in inference, intuition, and the approach of guesswork as preserving its dignity and adhering to its methodology and path?!.. And if the method of the Westerners in studying the life of Muhammad is not the scientific method that leads to truth as Husayn Haykal sees, nor the method that our Muslim predecessors followed, then the matter should end in one of two conclusions: either the Westerners believe in the prophethood of Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him) if Husayn Haykal sees that it is truth, or he himself denies his prophethood if he does not see it as truth. And we have seen how the choice of the Israeli radio station in Ramadan of this year fell upon this book specifically, to broadcast from it passages of the prophetic biography. Was that because the Israeli radio station is extremely keen not to broadcast anything from the life of Muhammad and his biography except on purely scientific foundations?!.. And suffice you as certainty of the high scientific value of a book that analyzes the life of the Messenger of God, that it is the book that the Jews choose to benefit from in covering religious programs for Muslims in their directed broadcast!.. Any intellectual knows that that (reformist) school was only established on one pillar, namely infatuation with the word (science) and lacking its content. And here we see today how science itself is taking on the task of sweeping away this (reformist) school through reason and research, and how the vision between science and miracle has become clearer than it was before. The period of infatuation has ended, and the eye has returned to look at the light with all its energy. And we began to look, and behold, reality mocks the prophecy of Muhammad Farid Wajdi when he said, while suffering from one of his emotional swoons with the word (science): 'The Islamic East, when it saw its religion embodied in the world of myths that religions had thrown into it wholesale at the hands of modern Western science, did not utter a word because it saw the matter as too great to attempt, but it internalized atheism and clung to it, convinced that it is the fate of all its brothers when they reach its scientific level.' (1) From an article published by Farid Wajdi in al-Ahram on 30-8-1937 in response to an article written by the scholar Mustafa Sabri, and see the story of the two articles in the book Mawqif al-Aql wa al-Ilm: 4-407. And he had not yet been appointed editor-in-chief of the journal al-Azhar known as (Nur al-Islam). But his ideas qualified him for this position later, succeeding the great scholar al-Allama al-`Azim al-Tabah [؟] Muhammad al-Khidr Husayn, as part of the reformist achievements that the British occupation had planned for the Azhar University specifically and Egyptian society in general (see p. 223 of this book). And no doubt he concealed these ideas after he became editor-in-chief of the great Islamic journal speaking in the name of al-Azhar, and kept them under his tongue for a period.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a sustained polemical critique by Buti against certain reformist Muslim thinkers who uncritically adopted Western scientific methodology and used the word 'science' as a pretext to reject miracles and the supernatural. Buti begins by describing how the British exploited this tendency, convincing people that 'science' requires denying miracles. He then expresses pity for the contradictory ideas in their books, which are full of 'science' but devoid of its true meaning. He specifically attacks Husayn Haykal's book 'Hayat Muhammad', noting that Haykal claims to follow the 'scientific method' by rejecting even authentic hadith from Bukhari and Muslim for the sake of science. Buti finds this absurd: Haykal considers reliance on Bukhari a deviation from scientific caution, yet he follows Western guesswork and inference. Buti then presents a logical dilemma: if the Western method is truly scientific and leads to truth, then it should compel Westerners to accept Muhammad's prophethood; if not, then Haykal himself should deny the prophethood. Buti further highlights that an Israeli radio station chose Haykal's book for Ramadan broadcasts, sarcastically asking if this is because it reflects 'scientific' foundations. He argues that this proves the book's worthlessness from a Muslim perspective. Buti then identifies the root of the reformist school: infatuation with the word 'science' without its substance. He claims that now, true science itself is sweeping away that school, and the relationship between science and miracles is clearer. He concludes by mocking Muhammad Farid Wajdi's prophecy that the Islamic East would embrace atheism upon reaching Western scientific levels. Buti includes a lengthy footnote about Farid Wajdi's later concealment of these ideas after becoming editor of an Azhar journal, implying hypocrisy. Throughout, Buti maintains that genuine science does not contradict Islam or miracles; the problem is a superficial and self-contradictory understanding of 'science'.

Key Terms
الطريقة العلمية (scientific method)
محمد فريد وجدي (Muhammad Farid Wajdi)
حسين هيكل (Husayn Haykal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That rejecting authentic hadith is necessary for a scientific approach.
Correction: Buti argues that true scientific caution would rely on authentic sources, not discard them.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what two conclusions must follow from Haykal's acceptance of the Western method as the scientific method?
A) Either the Westerners must accept the prophethood of Muhammad, or Haykal must deny it.
B) Either Haykal must reject all hadith, or he must accept all hadith.
C) Either the Western method is scientific, or it is not.
D) Either the book is valid, or it is not.

Key Takeaway
Buti exposes the inconsistency of rejecting authentic hadith in the name of science, showing it leads to a logical dilemma about prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever rejected a well-authenticated religious teaching because it seemed to conflict with your modern assumptions, without honestly examining whether those assumptions are themselves well-founded? What would it take for you to trust divine revelation over contemporary consensus?
?
Buti exposes a logical dilemma: if you claim a method leads to truth but it fails to affirm prophethood, you are inconsistent. In your own life, are there beliefs you hold that are logically inconsistent with your actions or other beliefs? Are you willing to follow the truth wherever it leads, even if it means admitting you were wrong?
?
Haykal prides himself on his 'scientific' approach, yet Buti shows it is based on guesswork. Where do you rely on the approval of others (like 'the West') to feel intellectually respectable? Could your desire to be seen as rational be preventing you from accepting clear truths from revealed sources?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
7 min
The Irony of Israeli Selection and the Collapse of Reformism
Buti uses Israeli radio and Farid Wajdi's prophecy to argue reformism is collapsing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti uses the Israeli radio station's choice of Haykal's book as evidence of its shortcomings, and how he argues that true science itself sweeps away the reformist school.

Core Idea
The reformist school collapses because its infatuation with 'science' lacks substance, as shown by the irony of Israeli endorsement.

Buti continues his critique by pointing out that an Israeli radio station chose Haykal's book for Ramadan broadcasts, sarcastically suggesting this reflects its 'scientific value'. He then argues that the reformist school was built only on infatuation with the word 'science' and lacked its content. Finally, he claims that true science now refutes the reformists, and he mocks Muhammad Farid Wajdi's prophecy of inevitable atheism.

Guided Path
1
Read the Israeli radio example
Read the passage where Buti mentions the Israeli radio station choosing Haykal's book. Consider the sarcasm.
Buti uses the example to undermine the book's credibility.
2
Understand the critique of reformist school
Buti says the school was based on infatuation with 'science' and lack of substance. How does he say science itself is now refuting them?
He claims the period of infatuation is over.
3
Examine the prophecy of Farid Wajdi
Buti mocks Farid Wajdi's prediction that the Islamic East would embrace atheism upon reaching Western scientific levels. What is Buti's point?
Buti implies that reality has shown the opposite.
