Commentary
This passage is a sustained polemical critique by Buti against certain reformist Muslim thinkers who uncritically adopted Western scientific methodology and used the word 'science' as a pretext to reject miracles and the supernatural. Buti begins by describing how the British exploited this tendency, convincing people that 'science' requires denying miracles. He then expresses pity for the contradictory ideas in their books, which are full of 'science' but devoid of its true meaning. He specifically attacks Husayn Haykal's book 'Hayat Muhammad', noting that Haykal claims to follow the 'scientific method' by rejecting even authentic hadith from Bukhari and Muslim for the sake of science. Buti finds this absurd: Haykal considers reliance on Bukhari a deviation from scientific caution, yet he follows Western guesswork and inference. Buti then presents a logical dilemma: if the Western method is truly scientific and leads to truth, then it should compel Westerners to accept Muhammad's prophethood; if not, then Haykal himself should deny the prophethood. Buti further highlights that an Israeli radio station chose Haykal's book for Ramadan broadcasts, sarcastically asking if this is because it reflects 'scientific' foundations. He argues that this proves the book's worthlessness from a Muslim perspective. Buti then identifies the root of the reformist school: infatuation with the word 'science' without its substance. He claims that now, true science itself is sweeping away that school, and the relationship between science and miracles is clearer. He concludes by mocking Muhammad Farid Wajdi's prophecy that the Islamic East would embrace atheism upon reaching Western scientific levels. Buti includes a lengthy footnote about Farid Wajdi's later concealment of these ideas after becoming editor of an Azhar journal, implying hypocrisy. Throughout, Buti maintains that genuine science does not contradict Islam or miracles; the problem is a superficial and self-contradictory understanding of 'science'.

Key Terms
محمد فريد وجدي (Muhammad Farid Wajdi)
المدرسة الإصلاحية (reformist school)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the reformist school represents a scientifically advanced approach.
Correction: Buti argues they lacked substance and that true science refutes them.

Checkpoint
Why does Buti consider the Israeli radio station's choice of Haykal's book as evidence against the reformists?
A) Because the book was banned in Arab countries.
B) Because Israeli endorsement shows the book serves Zionist interests, not Islamic truth.
C) Because the book was written by an Israeli.
D) Because the station only broadcasts scientific content.

Key Takeaway
The reformist school is self-defeating: its infatuation with 'science' lacks substance, and even science itself now refutes their positions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself defending Islam using arguments borrowed from modern science, are you actually trusting the same authority that the secular world uses to undermine revelation? Examine your heart: do you rely on 'scientific proofs' because you fear that the Qur'an alone is not enough?
?
The Israeli radio chose a reformist book enthusiastically. If the enemies of Islam endorse your method of presenting Islam, should that not frighten you? What does that say about the method itself? Are you willing to reconsider any of your own approaches?
?
Buti says the reformist school was built on infatuation with the word 'science' without its content. In your own study of Islam, do you ever find yourself enamored with terms like 'science', 'rational', 'progressive' while missing the actual substance of faith? What would it mean for you to abandon that infatuation today?

Refutation of Multiple Adams Claim
Buti refutes the Sufi claim of multiple Adams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Sufi claim of many Adams before the Adam of the Quran is rejected as baseless conjecture in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Claims about multiple Adams are pure conjecture, not grounded in revelation or reason.

Buti warns against entertaining speculative Sufi claims that the Adam mentioned in the Quran was preceded by many others. He argues that such assertions rest solely on imagination, lacking any definitive scriptural or rational evidence. This lesson examines that refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Buti dismisses the claim as based on 'pure conjecture' (al-hads al-mujarrad).
2
Identify the basis of the claim
Buti states the claim is not supported by a definitive report (khabar sadiq qat'i) nor by a certain rational proof. Reflect on why these are the two sources of knowledge in Islam.
3
Understand the tone
Buti uses a strong admonition: 'Woe to you, do not pay attention...' This shows the seriousness of deviating from established sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإياك أن تلتفت إلى ما يقوله بعض المتصوفة ، من زعم أن آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام المذكور قصة خلقه في القرآن - كان مسبوقاً بأوادم كثيرين غيره . ثم يذهبون يجرون ذيل الخيال في تفصيل الحديث عن ذلك فهذا الادعاء مبني على الحدس المجرد ، لا يدعمه دليل من الخبر الصادق القطعي ولا برهان يقيني من النظر العلمي . ومن الأدب مع كتاب الله تعالى (1) من العجيب المضحك أن بعض الملاحدة أرادوا أن يزعموا أن في القرآن تناقضاً ، فعكفوا على البحث عن ذلك .. ثم اهتدوا إلى هذا التناقض في هذا الذي يقوله عن أصل الإنسان : مرة يقول إنه مخلوق من تراب ، ومرة من صلصال ، ومرة من حمأ مسنون كالتناقض الذي يقع فيه من يقول : إن هذا البيت مبني من تراب من طين من آجر ! .. وإذا فقد الإنسان حريته حتى أصبحت ملك سادته ، فلا عجب أن يفقد عقله أيضاً ، فيفكر وهو يفكر برغبة غيره .
And beware of turning attention to what some Sufis say, of the claim that Adam, peace be upon him, whose story of creation is mentioned in the Quran, was preceded by many other Adams. Then they go dragging the tail of imagination in detailing talk about that. So this claim is based on pure conjecture, not supported by evidence from a definitive truthful report nor by a certain proof from scientific consideration. And from respect for the Book of God Almighty: (1) It is amusingly strange that some atheists wanted to claim that there is a contradiction in the Quran, so they devoted themselves to searching for that... then they stumbled upon this contradiction in what it says about the origin of man: sometimes it says he is created from dust, sometimes from sounding clay, sometimes from altered black mud—like the contradiction that occurs when someone says: this house is built from earth, from clay, from brick! ... And when a man loses his freedom until he becomes the property of his masters, it is no wonder that he also loses his mind, so he thinks while he thinks at the desire of others.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage refutes two claims. First, the Sufi claim of multiple Adams is pure conjecture (hads mujarrad) without support from definitive revelation or certain rational proof. Second, in a footnote, Buti ridicules atheists who allege a contradiction in the Quran's descriptions of human creation (dust, clay, mud), arguing that these are stages or types, just as a house can be described as built from earth, clay, or brick without contradiction. The atheists' loss of freedom leads to loss of independent thought.

Key Terms
أوادم كثيرين
الحدس المجرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Buti say is the basis for the claim that many Adams existed?
A) Definitive reports
B) Pure conjecture
C) Rational proofs
D) Consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
The claim of multiple Adams is rejected because it relies on pure conjecture, lacking support from definitive revelation or certain rational proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time you intuitively believed something about your faith because it 'felt right' or came from a respected spiritual figure, without checking the Quran or Sunnah. Will you now actively verify such beliefs, and what first step will you take this week?
?
Buti calls the claim of multiple Adams 'dragging the tail of imagination.' Where in your own religious practice might imagination be replacing solid knowledge—perhaps in assumptions about the unseen, the end times, or the lives of the prophets? Commit today to replacing one imagined notion with a fact from revelation.
?
This lesson insists that religious claims must be supported by definitive evidence or certain rational proof. Does your personal faith rest on such a foundation, or have you inherited beliefs without scrutiny? Write down one belief you will investigate to ensure it meets this standard.

The Alleged Contradiction in Creation Descriptions
Buti refutes the alleged Quranic contradiction about human creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran's varying descriptions of human creation (dust, clay, mud) are not contradictions but complementary accounts.

Core Idea
Different descriptions of creation are like saying a house is built from earth, clay, or brick — all true at different stages.

Buti addresses atheists who claim the Quran contradicts itself by describing human creation as from dust, clay, and mud. He uses a simple analogy: a house can be described as built from earth, clay, or brick without contradiction, because these refer to stages or materials. This lesson unpacks that refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the atheist claim
Buti presents the objection: the Quran seems to say man was created from dust, then from clay, then from mud. Atheists call this a contradiction.
2
Study Buti's analogy
Buti compares this to saying a house is built from earth, then clay, then brick. These are not contradictions but different stages or types of material.
3
Reflect on the deeper point
Buti concludes with a remark about loss of freedom leading to loss of independent thought — a jab at atheists who parrot claims without thinking.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Misconception: The Quran contradicts itself by saying man was created from dust, clay, and mud.

?

?
If an atheist friend proposes a supposed contradiction like this one, do you have the confidence to respond from your own understanding of this lesson? What would stop you from defending the Quran's perfection?
?
Buti says when a person loses freedom, he loses his mind. Are there areas in your life where you think not because you are free but because you follow the desires of others? Will you repent and commit to thinking for the sake of truth, even if it is uncomfortable?

The Contradiction of Rejecting Jinn While Accepting Séances
Al-Buti criticizes pseudo-Muslims who reject jinn due to lack of sensory evidence yet credulously accept spiritism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Buti's critique of the inconsistency in some Muslims who reject jinn based on sensory absence yet uncritically accept spiritism, and how he traces this to blind imitation of intellectual trends.

Core Idea
Rejecting jinn without evidence while embracing séances is not science but blind imitation.

Al-Buti addresses a peculiar inconsistency in some contemporary Muslims. They reject the Qur'anic reality of jinn because they cannot sense them, yet they embrace modern spiritism and séances without any scientific proof. In this passage, he exposes the root of this contradiction as blind imitation of ideological trends, not rational inquiry.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two attitudes
Read the passage and note how al-Buti contrasts the rejection of jinn with the acceptance of spirit séances by the same group.
Notice that both are based on following authority, not evidence.
2
Examine the accusation of foolishness
Al-Buti calls this stance 'astonishing foolishness'. What is the basis for this judgment? He says the only 'proof' for rejecting jinn is ignorance.
3
Trace the pattern of imitation
Al-Buti describes how these Muslims first uncritically accepted the claim that belief in jinn is animism, then later accepted spiritism when their masters promoted it. Track the sequence of events.
The key term is 'taqlid' (imitation) and 'ghazw fikri' (intellectual invasion).
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider what this critique teaches about the proper approach to Islamic beliefs: they must be based on revelation and reason, not on following intellectual fashions.
True iman requires intellectual integrity and consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير أن السخف العجيب إنما يكمن عند من يزعم أنه مسلم يؤمن بالله ورسوله وكتابه ، ثم يمضي يجادلك ، أو يجادل القرآن بتعبير أصح ، في وجود الجن مثلاً . ولا دليل يخاصمك به إلا أنه لم ير الجن ولم يحس بهم ، أي لا دليل له يخاصمك به إلا مجرد جهله كما قلنا والمقالة في جذورها ، مجرد تقليد ومحاكاة ، لمحترفي الغزو الفكري ضد الإسلام وأهله . فقد ألقوا الآذان إليهم ، فسمعوهم يقولون : إن الاعتقاد بالجن والشياطين والملائكة ، إنما هو من ( الإحيائية ) والخرافات التي كانت سائدة عند العرب ، فدعا إليها بعد ذلك محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام باسم الدين والإسلام ..! فأحنوا رؤوسهم لما سمعوا وأغمضوا العين والعقل عن التفكر في دليل هذه الدعوى وبواعثها وبراهينها العلمية ، ثم انطلقوا يرددون هذا الكلام ، دون أن يختلف أي اختلاف عن صوت سادتهم !.. ثم لما عاد أولئك السادة أنفسهم يتحدثون عن الأرواح وقصة تحضيرها وكيفية مناجاتها ، عاد هؤلاء مرة أخرى يستمعون ، وعادوا مرة أخرى ينغضون رؤوسهم مؤمنين معتقدين ، دون أن يكشفوا غطاء العقل لأي تأمل أو برهان علمي . ثم انطلقوا هذه المرة يعتقدون بالأرواح ، ويعلمون الناس السبيل إلى تحضيرها ومكالمتها واستكشاف خفايا الماضي السحيق والمستقبل البعيد بواسطتها (١)
However, the astonishing foolishness lies in the one who claims to be a Muslim believing in Allah, His Messenger, and His Book, then proceeds to argue with you—or more precisely, argues with the Qur'an—about the existence of jinn, for example. And he has no proof to challenge you with except that he has not seen the jinn nor perceived them, i.e., he has no proof to challenge you with except mere ignorance, as we said. And the issue in its roots is mere imitation and mimicry of the professional intellectual invasion against Islam and its people. They lent their ears to them, hearing them say that belief in jinn, devils, and angels is part of animism and superstitions that were prevalent among the Arabs, then afterwards Muhammad (peace be upon him) called to them in the name of religion and Islam! So they bowed their heads when they heard and closed their eyes and minds to reflecting on the proof of this claim and its motives and scientific evidences, then they went about repeating this talk, without differing in any way from the voice of their masters! Then when those same masters themselves began to talk about spirits and the story of their séance and how to communicate with them, these people once again listened, and once again nodded their heads believing and convinced, without uncovering the cover of the mind for any reflection or scientific proof. Then this time they went about believing in spirits, and teaching people the way to summon them and speak with them and uncover the secrets of the distant past and far future through them.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a critique of a specific group: Muslims who reject the existence of jinn based solely on lack of sensory perception, yet embrace spiritism and séances without evidence. Al-Buti calls this 'astonishing foolishness' ('سخف عجيب'). He traces the root of this inconsistency to blind imitation ('تقليد ومحاكاة') of those engaged in intellectual warfare against Islam. First, these Muslims uncritically accepted the claim that belief in jinn and angels is mere 'animism' ('الإحيائية') and superstition, echoing their intellectual masters. Then, when the same masters turned around and promoted séances and spirit communication, these people again followed without applying critical thought. The result: they reject the Qur'anically attested reality of jinn based on sensory absence, but accept spiritism—which also lacks scientific proof—based on the authority of those same masters. Al-Buti highlights the contradiction and the abdication of reason.

Key Terms
سخف (foolishness)
تقليد (imitation)
غزو فكري (intellectual invasion)
إحيائية (animism)
تحضير الأرواح (spirit séance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That rejecting jinn based on lack of sensory evidence is rational, while accepting spiritism without evidence is not; both are equally unscientific.
Correction: Al-Buti shows that both stances stem from blind imitation, not independent reasoning; one cannot reject one unseen based on sensoryism while accepting another unseen without evidence.

Checkpoint
According to al-Buti, what is the root cause of the contradictory stance of those who reject jinn but accept spirit séances?
A) Genuine scientific inquiry.
B) Blind imitation of intellectual trends.
C) Deep personal experience.
D) Careful study of Islamic texts.

Key Takeaway
Blind imitation of intellectual trends leads to contradictory beliefs; true faith requires evidence and consistency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life have you accepted an idea because it came from an authoritative source (a professor, a trend, a 'master') without stopping to examine it against the Qur'an and Sunnah? Where is your 'blind imitation' hiding?
?
When you feel embarrassed to affirm a clear truth from Allah's Book—like the existence of jinn—because of the mockery of modern intellectuals, whose approval are you really seeking? Are you willing to be called 'foolish' by the world but truthful before Allah?
?
Have you ever applied a double standard: demanding rigorous evidence for Islamic teachings while uncritically embracing secular or spiritual claims? What would it take for you to apply the same epistemic standard to all truth claims, starting today?

The Fallacy of 'Science Abrogates Religion'
Rhetorically refutes the claim that space age abrogated religion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rhetorical refutation of the claim that scientific progress abrogates religion, and recognize the fallacy of those who make such claims while being detached from actual scientific work.

Core Idea
Boastful claims that science abrogates religion often come from idle followers, not scientists.

This passage concludes the discussion of cosmic certainties by addressing a modern objection: that the space age has rendered religion obsolete. The author responds with rhetorical force, exposing the inconsistency and hypocrisy of such claims. Before we explore his words, consider how often we hear similar arguments today.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then its English translation. Let the author's tone and rhythm come through.
Notice the opening expression of wonder: 'And if you wonder, then wonder...'
2
Identify the target group
Who is being refuted? The author describes them as 'slaves of the East and West' who are mired in laziness and stagnation.
These are not the scientists themselves but those who boast on their behalf.
3
Analyze the rhetorical devices
Note the sarcasm: 'as if they are the ones conquering space' and the absurd image of wings growing from their sides.
The author uses exaggeration to highlight the emptiness of their claim.
4
Understand the core argument
The claimants are not actually engaged in science; they are boastful followers. Their claim that science has 'debunked myths' is baseless.
The final sentence reveals the real consequence: they pretend to have discovered God's kingdom and concluded atheism.
5
Reflect on faith and science
Consider how true scientific inquiry does not negate faith; rather, it magnifies the Creator. The author warns against being deceived by cultural trends.
This lesson guards against the misconception that science and religion are inherently contradictory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن تعجب، فعجب لعبيد الشرق والغرب إذ تراهم يتشدقون - وقد اثاقلوا إلى أرض من الكسل واللهو والخمول - بأن عصر الفضاء قد نسخ الدين، وأن الرقي العلمي قد كشف الأساطير .. يقولون هذا في نشوة تهز أعطافهم، وكأنهم هم الذين يغزون الفضاء ويسبحون حول الكواكب؛ أو كأنّ هذه الجعجعة ستخلق في جنبي كل منهم جناحين يقتلعان جذوره من تربة الدعة والخمول إلى عنان السماء، أو إلى حيث تسبح النجوم والأفلاك .! . أو كأنهم بذلك قد اكتشفوا ملكوت الله كله فأيقنوا أن لا خالق ولا إله !!.
And if you wonder, then wonder at the slaves of the East and West when you see them boast—while they have sunk into a land of laziness, amusement, and stagnation—saying that the space age has abrogated religion, and that scientific progress has debunked myths. They say this in an ecstasy that shakes their shoulders, as if they are the ones who are conquering space and swimming around the planets; or as if this clatter will create wings on the sides of each of them, uprooting them from the soil of comfort and stagnation to the expanse of the sky, or to where the stars and spheres swim; or as if they have thereby discovered all of God's dominion and become certain that there is no Creator and no god.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This final passage is a rhetorical refutation of those who claim that the space age has abrogated religion. The author expresses astonishment at such people, whom he calls 'slaves of the East and West,' who are themselves mired in laziness and stagnation but boast as though they personally have achieved space exploration. He mocks their empty claims, suggesting that their boastful talk will not literally give them wings to fly. The climax is that they act as if they have discovered all of God's kingdom and have become certain that there is no Creator or god—a clear reference to atheism. This lesson serves as a warning against being deceived by scientific progress into denying religion.

Key Terms
عصر الفضاء
نسخ الدين
أساطير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Scientific progress (the space age) has abrogated religion and proven its teachings to be myths.
Correction: The author shows that such claims are made by people who are not themselves scientists, but are boastful and idle followers. True scientific inquiry does not negate faith; rather, it reveals the grandeur of creation.

Checkpoint
What does the author accuse those who say 'the space age has abrogated religion' of being characterized by?
A) Scientific excellence.
B) Laziness and stagnation.
C) True faith.
D) Intellectual humility.

Key Takeaway
The claim that science abrogates religion is often made by those who are not genuinely engaged in scientific work but are merely caught up in cultural trends.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone claim that science has debunked religious beliefs, do you immediately accept it without examining the speaker's credentials or your own understanding? How can you actively resist being a passive follower like the 'slaves of the East and West'?
?
Think of a time you boasted about human progress or modern achievements to justify neglecting your religious duties. Did you personally contribute to that progress, or were you merely riding on others' work? What concrete step can you take today to realign your efforts with faith?
?
The author mocks empty talk that cannot sprout wings. In what areas of your life do you rely on fashionable slogans (e.g., 'science proves...' or 'modernity has moved past religion') to avoid deep thinking or personal accountability? Will you commit to investigating such claims with the same rigor you would expect from a true scientist?

Refuting a Wahhabi Critique of Hanafi Fiqh
Refutes a Wahhabi critic who disparaged Hanafi fiqh as contrary to Sharia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Dr. al-Buti refutes the accusation that Hanafi fiqh is separate from the Islamic Sharia and the importance of respecting the ijtihad of the Imams.

Core Idea
Hanafi fiqh derives from Quran and Sunnah; insulting it insults the Sharia itself.

In this passage, Dr. al-Buti responds to a Wahhabi critic who mocked Hanafi fiqh, implying it is not based on the Book and Sunnah. The author defends the integrity of Hanafi ijtihad and condemns such partisanship, calling for unity and forgiveness among Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Read the critic's quote
Read the quote from the Wahhabi critic that triggered this response. Notice how he distinguishes Hanafi fiqh from Sharia.
The critic wrote: 'Jesus rules by our Sharia, not by Hanafi fiqh.'
2
Understand the refutation
See how the author refutes by accusing the critic of equating Hanafi fiqh with the Torah or Gospel, which is a grave insult.
3
Examine the defense of Abu Hanifa
The author rhetorically asks if Abu Hanifa called people to abandon Sharia, and praises his ijtihad as derived from Quran and Sunnah.
4
Reflect on the concluding dua
The passage ends with a prayer for protection from grudges and for embodying forgiveness towards fellow Muslims.
This dua underscores the value of unity and respect.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتب أحد الوهابيين من خصوم السلف ، في تعليق له ، بمناسبة هذا البحث ما نصه : « هذا صريح في أن عيسى عليه السلام يحكم بشرعنا وبمقتضى الكتاب والسنة ، لا بغيرها من الإنجيل أو الفقه الحنفي ونحوه » ! .. إنك لترى أنه يقرر ، بصريح العبارة ، من خلال سخريته بالفقه الحنفي أنه عير الشريعة الإسلامية ، وإنما هو شيء آخر كالذي يسمى اليوم بالتوراة أو الإنجيل ! .. فأبو حنيفة رحمه الله إنما دعا الناس ، بزعمه ، إلى نبذ الشريعة الإسلامية والأخذ بفقهه بدلاً منها !! فهل من مسلم يتمتع بشيء من تقوى الله تعالى يتفوه بهذا الكلام الظالم الوقح ، في حق سلف هذه الأمة وإمام من أئمة علماء المسلمين ؟! وإنا لنعلم أن هذا الرجل ، أو ناشر الكتاب الذي ورد فيه الافتراء العجيب ، وقد تلقى مذكرات علماء المسلمين في أنحاء العالم الإسلامي ، تنبه إلى ضرورة شطب هذا اللغو ، فمـا أصـاخ واحد منهما إلى التذكير بهذا الحق وأبى كل منهما إلا أن يجعل من نفسه مطية ذلولاً للعصبية
كثيرة من
الشنعاء .
فالله المستعان أن ينتصر لعباده الذين ما آلوا جهداً في استخراج أحكام الشريعة الإسلامية من الكتاب والسنة ، فكانت اجتهاداتهم هي حكم الله تعالى في حقهم ، وحق كل من استرشدوا بعلمهم ممن لم يسعهم إلا تقليد الأئمة وأتباعهم ، يستوي في ذلك ما أصابوا فيه من تلك الاجتهادات وما أخطأوا . والله المستعان أن يعافينا من الضغائن والأحقاد تجاه سائر إخواننا المسلمين ، فضلاً عن السلف الصالح وأئمة المسلمين ، وأن يجعلنا من المتحققين بصفات أولئك الذين قال عنهم : « والذينَ جاؤوا مِنْ بَعدِهِمْ يَقولونَ رَبَّنا اغفر لنا ولإخواننا الَّذينَ سبقونا بالإيمان ، وَلا تَجْعَل في قُلوبنا غلا لِلَّذِينَ آمَنوا رَبَّنَا إِنَّكَ رَؤوف رحيمٌ ﴾ [ الحشر : ١٠ ] .
One of the Wahhabis, from the adversaries of the Salaf, wrote in a comment of his, on the occasion of this research, the following: 'This is explicit that Jesus, peace be upon him, rules by our Sharia and according to the Book and the Sunnah, not by other than them like the Gospel or Hanafi fiqh and the like'! ... You see that he states, in explicit terms, through his mockery of Hanafi fiqh, that it is a disgrace to the Islamic Sharia, and that it is something else like what is today called the Torah or the Gospel!! So did Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, call people, in his claim, to abandon the Islamic Sharia and take his fiqh instead of it?! Is there any Muslim who possesses any piety towards Allah Almighty who would utter this unjust and insolent speech regarding the Salaf of this Ummah and the Imam of the scholars of the Muslims?! We certainly know that this man, or the publisher of the book containing the amazing slander, who received memoranda from the scholars of the Muslims across the Islamic world, warning of the necessity of striking out this nonsense, neither of them heeded the reminder of this truth, and each refused except to make himself a docile mount for blind partisanship. So Allah is the One whose help is sought to give victory to His servants who spared no effort in deriving the rulings of the Islamic Sharia from the Book and the Sunnah, and their ijtihadat were the ruling of Allah for them and for everyone who sought guidance from their knowledge, for those whom only following the Imams and their followers was possible, equal in that what was correct of those ijtihadat and what was mistaken. And Allah is the One whose help is sought to protect us from grudges and hatreds towards all our fellow Muslims, not to mention the pious predecessors and Imams of the Muslims, and to make us among those who embody the qualities of those about whom He said: 'And those who came after them say: Our Lord, forgive us and our brothers who preceded us in faith, and do not put in our hearts any rancor towards those who have believed. Our Lord, indeed You are Kind and Merciful.' [Surah al-Hashr, 10].
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a polemical footnote that refutes a specific claim made by a Wahhabi critic. The critic had commented that Jesus rules by the Sharia and not by Hanafi fiqh, implying that Hanafi fiqh is something separate. The author strongly rejects this, accusing the critic of mocking and disparaging the Islamic Sharia itself by equating Hanafi fiqh with the Gospel or Torah. The author then defends Imam Abu Hanifa, arguing that he did not call people to abandon Sharia but rather derived rulings from Quran and Sunnah. The author expresses outrage at such slander against the Salaf and the Imams of Muslims. He notes that despite receiving protests from scholars worldwide, both the author and publisher persisted in their error due to blind partisanship. The passage concludes with a dua for Allah to vindicate the true scholars who derived rulings through ijtihad, recognizing that even in error they fulfilled their duty, and asks for protection from sectarian hatred and for the quality of forgiveness as mentioned in the Quranic verse.

Key Terms
الوهابيين
السلف
أبو حنيفة
الاجتهاد
تقليد الأئمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Hanafi fiqh is not based on Quran and Sunnah, and is separate from the Islamic Sharia.
Correction: Hanafi fiqh is derived from Quran and Sunnah through ijtihad; it is a valid school of Islamic jurisprudence.

Checkpoint
What accusation did the Wahhabi critic make against Abu Hanifa?
A) That Abu Hanifa denied the Sunnah.
B) That Abu Hanifa called people to abandon the Islamic Sharia and follow his fiqh instead.
C) That Abu Hanifa was not a scholar.
D) That Abu Hanifa invented new rulings.

Key Takeaway
Respecting the ijtihad of the Imams is part of respecting the Sharia, and partisanship leads to false accusations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever spoken lightly about a scholar or madhhab, even in private? How does this lesson's warning against 'insulting the Sharia itself' confront your own tongue?
?
The author describes the critic as making himself 'a docile mount for blind partisanship.' In what area of your life are you most vulnerable to defending your group without truth—and what would it cost you to stop?
?
The lesson ends with a prayer to be free from grudges. Is there a Muslim—especially one who differs from you in fiqh or aqeedah—against whom you hold resentment? Will you sincerely make du'a for them today, as the verse from al-Hashr teaches?

Buti's Defense of Hanafi Fiqh Against Wahhabi Criticism
Buti defends Imam Abu Hanifa against a Wahhabi charge of replacing Sharia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's defense of Hanafi fiqh against the accusation that it replaces Islamic Sharia, and appreciate the respect due to the Salaf and Imams.

Core Idea
Mocking a madhhab is mocking the scholars who derived it from Quran and Sunnah.

Buti encounters a Wahhabi critic who disparaged Hanafi fiqh, suggesting it is not part of Islamic Sharia. In this passionate response, Buti defends Imam Abu Hanifa and warns against sectarian prejudice. The passage calls for unity and respect among Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Pay attention to the tone and the flow of Buti's argument.
Notice how Buti quotes the critic before responding.
2
Identify the accusation and defense
Identify what the Wahhabi critic claimed about Hanafi fiqh and how Buti refutes it. Note that Buti equates the critic's mockery with slander against the Salaf.
The critic implied Hanafi fiqh is separate from Sharia.
3
Reflect on Buti's conclusion
Consider Buti's prayer for unity and forgiveness, and how he uses Quran 59:10 to emphasize respect for all Muslims and scholars.

(1) One of the Wahhabis, among the opponents of the Salaf, wrote in a comment of his, on the occasion of this research, the following text: 'This is explicit that Jesus, peace be upon him, judges by our law and according to the Book and the Sunnah, not by anything else from the Gospel or Hanafi fiqh or the like!' ... You see that he asserts, in explicit terms, through his mockery of Hanafi fiqh, that it is not the Islamic Sharia, but rather something else like what is called today the Torah or the Gospel! So Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, called people, according to his claim, to abandon the Islamic Sharia and to take his fiqh instead of it!! Is there any Muslim who possesses any piety towards Allah who would utter such unjust and insolent speech regarding the Salaf of this Ummah and an Imam among the Imams of the Muslim scholars?! And we know that this man, or the publisher of the book containing this strange slander, received memoranda from Muslim scholars throughout the Islamic world, reminding him of the necessity of deleting this nonsense. But not one of them heeded the reminder of this truth, and each of them insisted on making himself a submissive mount for ugly partisanship. So may Allah be the One sought for help to support His servants who spared no effort in deriving the rulings of Islamic Sharia from the Book and the Sunnah, so their ijtihad was the ruling of Allah regarding them and regarding all who sought guidance from their knowledge of those who could not do anything except taqlid of the Imams and their followers, equal in that what they were correct in from those ijtihads and what they were wrong. And may Allah be the One sought for help to protect us from resentments and hatreds towards all our fellow Muslims, let alone the righteous Salaf and the Imams of the Muslims, and to make us among those who realize the qualities of those about whom He said: 'And those who came after them, saying, "Our Lord, forgive us and our brothers who preceded us in faith, and put not in our hearts any resentment toward those who have believed. Our Lord, indeed You are Kind and Merciful."' [Al-Hashr: 10].
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a polemical footnote in which Buti responds to a Wahhabi critic who mocked Hanafi fiqh, claiming that it is separate from Islamic Sharia. The critic asserted that Jesus will judge only by Quran and Sunnah, not by Hanafi fiqh, implying that Hanafi fiqh is not part of Sharia. Buti denounces this as unjust and insolent, noting that it equates Hanafi fiqh with distorted scriptures. He defends Imam Abu Hanifa and the Salaf, stating that their ijtihad is indeed the ruling of Allah for those who follow them. He criticizes the publisher for ignoring reminders from scholars to delete such slander. The passage ends with a prayer for unity and forgiveness, quoting Quran 59:10.

Refutation of the Ahmadiyya Claim about the Promised Messiah
The author exposes the Ahmadiyya sect's false claims about a new prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ahmadiyya claim about a 'likeness of Jesus' as a new prophet contradicts Islamic teachings and is linked to an external plot.

Core Idea
The Ahmadiyya claim is not a legitimate prophecy but a colonial plot wrapped in false prophethood.

This passage exposes the origins and claims of the Ahmadiyya movement, revealing how its founder manipulated Islamic expectations of the Messiah. The author connects the movement's emergence to an English conspiracy and critiques its core deviation: the claim of a new prophet with independent revelation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Learn that the Ahmadiyya claim emerged from a group that allegedly sold its intellect to an English plot. This sets the stage for the refutation.
The author presents the claim as originating from a foreign conspiracy.
2
Identify the core claim
The founder claimed the promised Messiah is a 'likeness of Jesus' (مثيل عيسى), not Jesus himself, and that he would descend from heaven.
This distorts the Islamic belief that Jesus himself will return.
3
Observe the escalation
The founder then claimed to be an independent prophet with his own revelation like the Quran and invented miracles as proofs.
This contradicts the finality of prophethood with Muhammad (peace be upon him).
4
Note the symbolic renaming
The founder built a mosque in Qadian and named it al-Aqsa Mosque, and called his town 'Mecca of the Messiah', mimicking sacred sites.
This shows the attempt to create a parallel religious geography.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثانية: ذلك الخوض السخيف الذي خاضته فئة طاب لها أن تبيع عقلها لمخطط وكيد إنكليزي مكشوف، فقد قام قائمها يزعم أن الذي وعد الله بظهوره في الأرض هو مثيل عيسى وليس بعيسى نفسه، وأنه إنما يظهر في الأرض أن ينزل من السماء، وأنه السماء، وأنه هو ذلك المثيل الذي وعد الله بظهوره، فهو المسيح الموعود. ثم راح يزعم أنه نبي ورسول مستقل مؤيد بتشريع، ثم صاغ لنفسه وحياً كالقرآن، ومضى يختلق لنفسه معجزات يزعم أنها مؤيدات له، وابتني لنفسه مسجداً في بلدة (قاديان) وسماه المسجد الأقصى، وسمى بلدته: مكة المسيح.
The second issue: That foolish venture which a group undertook, that was pleased to sell its intellect to an exposed English plot and scheme. Its leader claimed that the one whom Allah promised to appear on earth is a likeness of Jesus, not Jesus himself, and that he only appears on earth to descend from heaven, and that he is heaven, and that he is that likeness whom Allah promised to appear, so he is the promised Messiah. Then he began to claim that he is an independent prophet and messenger supported by legislation, then he composed for himself a revelation like the Quran, and proceeded to invent for himself miracles claiming that they are proofs for him, and he built for himself a mosque in the town of Qadian and named it al-Aqsa Mosque, and named his town: Mecca of the Messiah.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage describes and refutes the claims of the Ahmadiyya movement. The author states that this group sold their intellect to an exposed English plot. Their leader claimed that the one Allah promised to appear on earth is a likeness of Jesus (not Jesus himself), and that this likeness would descend from heaven. The leader further claimed to be an independent prophet with a new revelation like the Quran and invented miracles. He built a mosque in Qadian and renamed it al-Aqsa Mosque, and called his town 'Mecca of the Messiah.' The author presents this as a clear deviation from Islamic teachings, noting its foreign origin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Ahmadiyya claim is a legitimate interpretation of Islamic prophecies.
Correction: The author shows it is based on a colonial plot and invalid claims to prophethood, contradicting the finality of prophethood in Islam.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the core claim of the Ahmadiyya leader about the promised Messiah?
A) He is Jesus himself returning to earth.
B) He is a likeness of Jesus, not Jesus himself, and is a new prophet.
C) He is an angel who will appear.
D) He is a descendant of Jesus.

Key Takeaway
The Ahmadiyya claim of a new prophet after Muhammad (peace be upon him) is a false innovation rooted in external conspiracy and contradicts core Islamic teachings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What would you say to someone who claims to receive new revelation from Allah after the Qur’an? How does this lesson equip you to recognize and reject such falsehood with certainty?
?
If a charismatic leader today performed ‘miracles’ and renamed a town after a holy site, would your iman be strong enough to identify the deception? Reflect on the markers of false prophethood mentioned in this passage.
?
The author calls the Ahmadiyya venture a 'foolish' sale of intellect to a colonial plot. Where are you most vulnerable to selling your intellect—through blind following, desire for novelty, or worldly influence? How will you guard your faith against such schemes?

Mirza Ghulam Ahmad's False Claims
Enumeration of Qadiani false claims and innovations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific false claims made by Mirza Ghulam Ahmad, including his claim to be the promised Messiah, a prophet with a revelation, and his distortions of Islamic teachings.

Core Idea
False prophets weave elaborate claims to deceive.

This passage details the false claims of Mirza Ghulam Ahmad, the founder of the Qadiani movement. He claimed to be the promised Messiah (a likeness of Jesus), an independent prophet with a revelation like the Quran, and he built a mosque and cemetery with sacred names. He also distorted the Quran and Sunnah through metaphorical interpretations. Understanding these claims helps us see how false movements arise.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on claims
Read the Arabic and translation listing Mirza's claims: messiah as likeness, prophethood, revelation, mosque, cemetery, etc.
Notice the specific terms like 'مسجد الأقصى' and 'مقبرة الجنة'.
2
Identify the types of claims
Categorize the claims: about person (likeness of Jesus), about status (prophet), about practices (mosque, burial), about scripture (revelation like Quran).
3
Reflect on the distortion
Note how he reinterpreted clear texts (zawaahir) as metaphorical to change laws.
This is a common tactic of false claimants.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثانية : ذلك الخوض السخيف الذي خاضته فئة طاب لها أن تبيع عقلها لمخطط وكيد إنكليزي مكشوف ، فقد قام قائمها يزعم أن الذي وعد الله بظهوره في الأرض هو مثيل عيسى وليس بعيسى نفسه ، وأنه إنما يظهر في الأرض أن ينزل من السماء ، وأنه السماء ، وأنه هو ذلك المثيل الذي وعد الله بظهوره ، فهو المسيح الموعود . ثم راح يزعم أنه نبي ورسول مستقل مؤيد بتشريع ، ثم صاغ لنفسه وحياً كالقرآن ، ومضى يختلق لنفسه معجزات يزعم أنها مؤيدات له ، وابتني لنفسه مسجداً في بلدة ( قاديان ( وسماه المسجد الأقصى ، وسمى بلدته : مكة المسيح وجعل مقبرة سماها مقبرة الجنة ، من دفن بها فهو من أهل الجنة وسمى أزواجه أمهات المؤمنين ، وراح يجمع من حوله الشيعة والأتباع بكل حيلة ووسيلة ، والاستعمار البريطاني من ورائه يدفعه ويغذيه ، ثم أعلن أن ظواهر الكتاب والسنة مصروفة إلى الاستعارات والكنايات والمجاز ، فأخذ يحرّف كما يشاء في شرع الكتاب والسنة وأحكامها . وكان من جملة هديه في ذلك ، أن الجهاد موضوع و منسوخ خاصة بالنسبة للإنكليز وذلك لموقفهم النبيل من المسلمين وحسن رعايتهم لهم !! ولم يزل على حاله تلك ، يدعي النبوة ويكذب على الله وأنبيـائـه ، ويضع نفسه للناس موضع المسيح عيسى ابن مريم ، إلى أن رماه قضاء الله تعالى بالهيضة ( داء الكوليرا ( ومات في بيت الخلاء ساقطاً على وجهه في أتعس حـالـة وأقبح منظر ، وكانت موتته هذه عبرة لأولي الأبصار . ذلك هو غلام أحمد القادياني الذي ولد عام ١٢٥٢ ومـات عام ١١٣٢٦) ولقد أخذ خلفاء هذا الدجال المضل يحاولون نشر ضلالات نبيهم هذا في مختلف البلاد ولابد أنك قد سمعت عن شراذم منهم هنا وهناك ، وعما توليهم بريطانيا في بلادها من الرعاية والتكريم . فإن لهم هناك معابد خاصة بهم ، ولهم ما لا يملكه غيرهم من أوجه النشاط لتغذية إفكهم وضلالاتهم !! وليس غرضنا من إطلاعك على هذه الضلالة مناقشتها وعَرضُ الدلائل على بطلانها ، فسخفها واضح بين لا يحتاج إلى بحث أو نظر ؛ ولكني قصدت أن تعلم كيف يقف عدو للإسلام من وراء كل نحلة أو دعوة باطلة ، ولقد برعت بريطانيا في الكيد للإسلام من وراء هذا الطريق كما لم يبرع في ذلك أي عدو آخر (۱) انظر كتاب التصريح بما تواتر من نزول المسيح ، وما كتبه في هذا الصدد محققه الأستاذ الجليل عبد الفتاح أبو غدة نقلاً عن الإمام الكشميري في مقدمة كتاب ( الإسلام في حياة عيسى عليه السلام ) ص ٣٨ - ٤٣
The second issue: That foolish talk in which a group indulged, pleased to sell their intellect to an open British plan and plot. For their proponent claimed that the one whom God promised to appear on earth is a likeness of Jesus, not Jesus himself, and that he only appears on earth... and that he is the heaven? and that he is that likeness whom God promised to appear, so he is the promised Messiah. Then he went on to claim that he is an independent prophet and messenger supported by legislation, then he fashioned for himself a revelation like the Quran, and proceeded to fabricate miracles for himself claiming they are supports for him, and he built for himself a mosque in the town of Qadian and named it Al-Aqsa Mosque, and named his town 'Mecca of the Messiah' and made a cemetery which he called the Garden of Paradise; whoever is buried there is among the people of Paradise, and he named his wives the Mothers of the Believers, and he began to gather around him followers by every trick and means, with British colonialism behind him pushing and nourishing him. Then he announced that the apparent meanings of the Book and Sunnah are turned to metaphors and metonymy and figurative speech, so he began to distort as he pleased the law of the Book and Sunnah and their rulings. Among his guidance in that was that jihad is suspended and abrogated especially with regard to the English, because of their noble stance towards Muslims and their good care of them!! He continued in his state, claiming prophethood and lying about God and His prophets, and presenting himself to people as the Messiah Jesus son of Mary, until the decree of God Almighty struck him with cholera and he died in the toilet, falling on his face in the most miserable state and worst appearance, and his death was a lesson for those with insight. That is Ghulam Ahmad Al-Qadiani who was born in 1252 and died in 1326? And indeed the successors of this deceptive false Messiah have attempted to spread the delusions of their prophet in various countries, and surely you have heard of small groups of them here and there, and of the care and honor that Britain gives them in their country. For they have there temples of their own, and they have what others do not have of forms of activity to feed their falsehood and delusions!! Our purpose in informing you of this falsehood is not to discuss it and present proofs of its invalidity, for its foolishness is clear and obvious and does not need research or consideration; but I intended that you know how an enemy of Islam stands behind every sect or false call, and Britain excelled in plotting against Islam through this way as no other enemy has excelled. (1) See book 'At-Tasreeh bima tawatara min nuzool al-Maseeh' and what its editor the noble professor Abdul Fattah Abu Ghuddah wrote in this regard quoting from Imam Al-Kashmiri in the introduction to the book 'Al-Islam fi Hayat Isa Alayhi as-Salam', pp. 38-43.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is an exposure of the Qadiani (Ahmadiyya) movement founded by Mirza Ghulam Ahmad. The author describes their false claims: that the promised Messiah is a likeness of Jesus, not Jesus himself; that Mirza claimed prophethood and a revelation like the Quran; that he built a mosque called Al-Aqsa and a cemetery called Paradise; that he abolished jihad towards the British; and that British colonialism supported him. The author narrates his ignominious death from cholera in a toilet. He then notes that his successors continue to propagate these delusions with British patronage. The author clarifies that his purpose is not to refute (since the falsehood is obvious) but to show how enemies of Islam use such movements as tools.

Key Terms
المسيح الموعود
غلام أحمد القادياني
مسجد الأقصى (في قاديان)
أمهات المؤمنين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Mirza Ghulam Ahmad was a reformer within Islam.
Correction: The passage shows he claimed prophethood and revelation, which contradicts the finality of prophethood in Islam.

Checkpoint
What did Mirza Ghulam Ahmad claim about the identity of the promised Messiah?
A) He is Jesus himself descending from heaven.
B) He is a likeness of Jesus, not Jesus himself.
C) He is a new prophet from God.
D) He is the Mahdi.

Key Takeaway
Mirza Ghulam Ahmad made multiple false claims to mimic prophethood and Islamic symbols, distorting core beliefs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about false prophets like Mirza Ghulam Ahmad, do you examine your own heart for the seeds of arrogance that lead people to elevate themselves? What safeguards have you placed in your life to ensure you never follow someone who distorts the Quran and Sunnah for their own gain?
?
The author exposes these claims as clear deceptions. Are there any areas in your life where you have accepted a distortion of Islamic teachings because it was convenient or appealing? Will you commit to investigating any teaching that feels 'too good to be true' against the Quran and Sunnah?
?
Mirza Ghulam Ahmad used religious symbols to gain followers. Are you attached to any symbols or practices that have become ends in themselves rather than means to worship Allah? How can you purify your intentions?

British Complicity and the Death of a False Messiah
Exposure of British backing and divine punishment of false prophet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how British colonialism supported Mirza Ghulam Ahmad and how his ignominious death served as a lesson, and the broader principle that enemies of Islam exploit false movements.

Core Idea
Enemies of Islam back false prophets to weaken faith.

This continuation of the passage focuses on the specific role of British colonialism in supporting Mirza Ghulam Ahmad, especially his abrogation of jihad against them. It then narrates his death from cholera in a toilet, which the author presents as a divine lesson. Finally, the author explains that his purpose is not debate but to show how enemies use such movements.

Guided Path
1
Read the British connection
Read the part about Mirza abrogating jihad for the British and British support.
Notice the sarcasm: 'because of their noble stance'.
2
Read the death narrative
Read the description of his death from cholera in a toilet.
The author presents this as a visible punishment.
3
Understand the author's purpose
Read the concluding lines where the author says he is not debating but exposing the enemy's tactic.
This reframes the entire passage.

?

?
Mirza died in a toilet, falling on his face—a humiliating end from Allah. If Allah exposed a false prophet in such a degrading way, what does that tell you about the certainty of divine justice? ?

The False Claims and Innovations of Ghulam Ahmad
Buti enumerates Ghulam Ahmad's false innovations and his reliance on British support.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific false claims made by Ghulam Ahmad al-Qadiyani and understand how he used deceptive innovations to attract followers.

Core Idea
Ghulam Ahmad invented a 'Paradise cemetery' and called his wives 'Mothers of the Believers' to fabricate religious legitimacy.

The passage describes how Ghulam Ahmad al-Qadiyani attempted to establish a new religious following by making outlandish claims. Buti exposes these tricks, showing how he created a mock paradise and claimed authority over his followers. This lesson examines those deceptive practices.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage describing Ghulam Ahmad's innovations. Notice the specific claims he made.
Pay attention to the names he gave to his cemetery and wives.
2
Identify the false claims
List the claims: 1) he designated a cemetery as Paradise, 2) he called his wives 'Ummahat al-Mu'minin', 3) he gathered followers with any means.
3
Understand the role of British support
Buti mentions that British colonialism was behind him, pushing and nurturing him. Why is this important?
This shows the political dimension of false religious movements.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why Buti includes these details. What does this teach us about false prophets?
The pattern of false claims often mimics authentic Islam to mislead.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجعل مقبرة سماها مقبرة الجنة، من دفن بها فهو من أهل الجنة وسمى أزواجه أمهات المؤمنين، وراح يجمع من حوله الشيعة والأتباع بكل حيلة ووسيلة، والاستعمار البريطاني من ورائه يدفعه ويغذيه، ثم أعلن أن ظواهر الكتاب والسنة مصروفة إلى الاستعارات والكنايات والمجاز، فأخذ يحرّف كما يشاء في شرع الكتاب والسنة وأحكامها. وكان من جملة هديه في ذلك، أن الجهاد موضوع ومنسوخ خاصة بالنسبة للإنكليز وذلك لموقفهم النبيل من المسلمين وحسن رعايتهم لهم!! ولم يزل على حاله تلك، يدعي النبوة ويكذب على الله وأنبيائه، ويضع نفسه للناس موضع المسيح عيسى ابن مريم، إلى أن رماه قضاء الله تعالى بالهيضة (داء الكوليرا) ومات في بيت الخلاء ساقطاً على وجهه في أتعس حال وأقبح منظر، وكانت موتته هذه عبرة لأولي الأبصار. ذلك هو غلام أحمد القادياني الذي ولد عام ١٢٥٢ ومات عام ١٣٢٦. ولقد أخذ خلفاء هذا الدجال المضل يحاولون نشر ضلالات نبيهم هذا في مختلف البلاد. ولابد أنك قد سمعت عن شراذم منهم هنا وهناك، وعما توليهم بريطانيا في بلادها من الرعاية والتكريم. فإن لهم هناك معابد خاصة بهم، ولهم ما لا يملكه غيرهم من أوجه النشاط لتغذية إفكهم وضلالاتهم!! وليس غرضنا من إطلاعك على هذه الضلالة مناقشتها وعرض الدلائل على بطلانها، فسخفها واضح بين لا يحتاج إلى بحث أو نظر؛ ولكني قصدت أن تعلم كيف يقف عدو للإسلام من وراء كل نحلة أو دعوة باطلة، ولقد برعت بريطانيا في الكيد للإسلام كما لم يبرع في ذلك أي عدو آخر للإسلام والمسلمين. ولو وقفت على تاريخ هذه الدولة وماضيها مع المسلمين عامة ومستعمراتها الإسلامية خاصة، لوقفت من ذلك على أمر يثير الدهشة في الرؤوس ويبعث العبرة في العقول.
And he made a cemetery which he called the cemetery of Paradise; whoever is buried in it is among the people of Paradise. And he called his wives the Mothers of the Believers. And he began gathering around him partisans and followers by every trick and means, with British colonialism behind him pushing and nurturing him. Then he announced that the outward meanings of the Book and the Sunnah are diverted to metaphors, metonymies, and figurative speech. So he began to distort as he wished in the law of the Book and the Sunnah and their rulings. Among his guidance in that was that jihad is abrogated and superseded, especially with respect to the English, because of their noble stance toward the Muslims and their good care for them!! And he continued in that state, claiming prophethood and lying about God and His prophets, and presenting himself to the people as the Messiah Jesus son of Mary, until the decree of God Almighty struck him with cholera (the disease of cholera) and he died in a toilet, falling on his face in the most wretched state and ugliest sight. And this death of his was a lesson for those of insight. That is Ghulam Ahmad al-Qadiyani, who was born in 1252 and died in 1326. And the successors of this deceiving Dajjal have taken to trying to spread the delusions of their prophet in various countries. And you must have heard of splinter groups of them here and there, and of the care and honor that Britain gives them in her land. For they have temples of their own there, and they have what others do not possess of aspects of activity to nourish their falsehood and delusions!! And our purpose in informing you of this delusion is not to discuss it and present proofs of its falsehood, for its silliness is clear and manifest, needing no investigation or reflection. Rather, I intended that you know how an enemy of Islam stands behind every heretical sect or false call. And Britain has excelled in plotting against Islam in this way as no other enemy of Islam and the Muslims has excelled. And if you were to study the history of this state and its past with Muslims in general and its Islamic colonies in particular, you would find therein a matter that causes astonishment in minds and brings lessons to intellects.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a historical and theological exposure of Ghulam Ahmad al-Qadiyani, the founder of the Qadiani sect. Buti begins by listing his false innovations: designating a cemetery as 'Paradise's cemetery', claiming his wives as 'Mothers of the Believers', and gathering followers with British backing. Buti then states that Ghulam Ahmad declared the outward meanings of Quran and Sunnah to be metaphorical, allowing him to distort rulings. A key example is his declaration that jihad is abrogated, especially against the English, due to their supposed benevolence. Buti describes his ongoing claims to prophethood and his self-identification as Jesus until God struck him with cholera, causing him to die ignominiously in a toilet. This death is presented as a divine lesson. Buti then notes the spread of the sect by successors and the support they receive from Britain. He clarifies that his aim is not to refute the sect's falsehood (which is self-evident) but to highlight how enemies of Islam support such false movements. He concludes by asserting Britain's exceptional role in plotting against Islam and urges reflection on their history with Muslims.

Key Terms
غلام أحمد القادياني
الاستعمار البريطاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Ghulam Ahmad call his cemetery?
A) Cemetery of the Righteous
B) Cemetery of Paradise
C) Cemetery of the Prophets
D) Cemetery of the Martyrs

Key Takeaway
False religious leaders often imitate authentic Islamic symbols to deceive followers, and external political powers may support them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter someone who uses religious symbols like 'Paradise' or 'Mothers of the Believers' for personal gain, do you feel drawn in by the familiarity or do you stop to verify their authenticity? How can you train yourself to discern genuine teachings from deceptive imitations?
?
This lesson shows that false leaders often combine religious claims with worldly power. In your own life, are you more impressed by a person's worldly influence (wealth, status, political backing) than by their adherence to truth? What would it take for you to reject a popular but false teacher?
?
Ghulam Ahmad's followers were deceived by his imitation of authentic Islamic concepts. When it comes to your own understanding of Islam, are you content with surface-level similarities, or do you actively seek deep, reliable knowledge from trustworthy sources? What concrete step will you take this week to strengthen your connection to authentic teachings?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
5 min
Distorting Divine Law: Ghulam Ahmad's Attack on Jihad
Buti exposes Ghulam Ahmad's distortion of Quran/Sunnah into metaphors and his abrogation of jihad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghulam Ahmad manipulated the interpretation of the Quran and Sunnah to abrogate jihad and serve colonial interests.

Core Idea
Declaring jihad abrogated was a key distortion to win British favor.

After establishing his authority, Ghulam Ahmad moved to alter core Islamic teachings. He claimed that the outward meanings of the Quran and Sunnah were merely metaphorical, allowing him to reinterpret laws as he wished. His most notorious change was the abrogation of jihad, especially against the British. This lesson examines that distortion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on distortion
Read the Arabic where Buti describes Ghulam Ahmad's declaration about metaphors and the abrogation of jihad.
Notice the claim: 'ظواهر الكتاب والسنة مصروفة إلى الاستعارات والكنايات والمجاز'.
2
Identify the method of distortion
He claimed that apparent meanings are not literal but metaphorical. This allowed him to change laws arbitrarily.
This is a common tactic of false reformers.
3
Focus on the abrogation of jihad
Specifically, he said jihad is abrogated, especially against the English, because of their good treatment of Muslims. Why is this ironic?
Buti uses exclamation marks to show the absurdity.
4
Connect to colonial support
Why would the British support such a teaching? How does it benefit them?
It disarms Muslims from defending themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجعل مقبرة سماها مقبرة الجنة، من دفن بها فهو من أهل الجنة وسمى أزواجه أمهات المؤمنين، وراح يجمع من حوله الشيعة والأتباع بكل حيلة ووسيلة، والاستعمار البريطاني من ورائه يدفعه ويغذيه، ثم أعلن أن ظواهر الكتاب والسنة مصروفة إلى الاستعارات والكنايات والمجاز، فأخذ يحرّف كما يشاء في شرع الكتاب والسنة وأحكامها. وكان من جملة هديه في ذلك، أن الجهاد موضوع ومنسوخ خاصة بالنسبة للإنكليز وذلك لموقفهم النبيل من المسلمين وحسن رعايتهم لهم!! ولم يزل على حاله تلك، يدعي النبوة ويكذب على الله وأنبيائه، ويضع نفسه للناس موضع المسيح عيسى ابن مريم، إلى أن رماه قضاء الله تعالى بالهيضة (داء الكوليرا) ومات في بيت الخلاء ساقطاً على وجهه في أتعس حال وأقبح منظر، وكانت موتته هذه عبرة لأولي الأبصار. ذلك هو غلام أحمد القادياني الذي ولد عام ١٢٥٢ ومات عام ١٣٢٦. ولقد أخذ خلفاء هذا الدجال المضل يحاولون نشر ضلالات نبيهم هذا في مختلف البلاد. ولابد أنك قد سمعت عن شراذم منهم هنا وهناك، وعما توليهم بريطانيا في بلادها من الرعاية والتكريم. فإن لهم هناك معابد خاصة بهم، ولهم ما لا يملكه غيرهم من أوجه النشاط لتغذية إفكهم وضلالاتهم!! وليس غرضنا من إطلاعك على هذه الضلالة مناقشتها وعرض الدلائل على بطلانها، فسخفها واضح بين لا يحتاج إلى بحث أو نظر؛ ولكني قصدت أن تعلم كيف يقف عدو للإسلام من وراء كل نحلة أو دعوة باطلة، ولقد برعت بريطانيا في الكيد للإسلام كما لم يبرع في ذلك أي عدو آخر للإسلام والمسلمين. ولو وقفت على تاريخ هذه الدولة وماضيها مع المسلمين عامة ومستعمراتها الإسلامية خاصة، لوقفت من ذلك على أمر يثير الدهشة في الرؤوس ويبعث العبرة في العقول.
And he made a cemetery which he called the cemetery of Paradise; whoever is buried in it is among the people of Paradise. And he called his wives the Mothers of the Believers. And he began gathering around him partisans and followers by every trick and means, with British colonialism behind him pushing and nurturing him. Then he announced that the outward meanings of the Book and the Sunnah are diverted to metaphors, metonymies, and figurative speech. So he began to distort as he wished in the law of the Book and the Sunnah and their rulings. Among his guidance in that was that jihad is abrogated and superseded, especially with respect to the English, because of their noble stance toward the Muslims and their good care for them!! And he continued in that state, claiming prophethood and lying about God and His prophets, and presenting himself to the people as the Messiah Jesus son of Mary, until the decree of God Almighty struck him with cholera (the disease of cholera) and he died in a toilet, falling on his face in the most wretched state and ugliest sight. And this death of his was a lesson for those of insight. That is Ghulam Ahmad al-Qadiyani, who was born in 1252 and died in 1326. And the successors of this deceiving Dajjal have taken to trying to spread the delusions of their prophet in various countries. And you must have heard of splinter groups of them here and there, and of the care and honor that Britain gives them in her land. For they have temples of their own there, and they have what others do not possess of aspects of activity to nourish their falsehood and delusions!! And our purpose in informing you of this delusion is not to discuss it and present proofs of its falsehood, for its silliness is clear and manifest, needing no investigation or reflection. Rather, I intended that you know how an enemy of Islam stands behind every heretical sect or false call. And Britain has excelled in plotting against Islam in this way as no other enemy of Islam and the Muslims has excelled. And if you were to study the history of this state and its past with Muslims in general and its Islamic colonies in particular, you would find therein a matter that causes astonishment in minds and brings lessons to intellects.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a historical and theological exposure of Ghulam Ahmad al-Qadiyani, the founder of the Qadiani sect. Buti begins by listing his false innovations: designating a cemetery as 'Paradise's cemetery', claiming his wives as 'Mothers of the Believers', and gathering followers with British backing. Buti then states that Ghulam Ahmad declared the outward meanings of Quran and Sunnah to be metaphorical, allowing him to distort rulings. A key example is his declaration that jihad is abrogated, especially against the English, due to their supposed benevolence. Buti describes his ongoing claims to prophethood and his self-identification as Jesus until God struck him with cholera, causing him to die ignominiously in a toilet. This death is presented as a divine lesson. Buti then notes the spread of the sect by successors and the support they receive from Britain. He clarifies that his aim is not to refute the sect's falsehood (which is self-evident) but to highlight how enemies of Islam support such false movements. He concludes by asserting Britain's exceptional role in plotting against Islam and urges reflection on their history with Muslims.

Key Terms
الكتاب والسنة
الاستعارات
الجهاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Ghulam Ahmad's interpretation was a legitimate reform that brought peace with colonial powers.
Correction: Buti shows that it was a deliberate distortion that contradicted clear Islamic texts and served colonial interests.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Ghulam Ahmad claim about the outward meanings of the Quran and Sunnah?
A) They are clear and literal
B) They are abrogated entirely
C) They are to be taken as metaphors and figurative speech
D) They are only for scholars

Key Takeaway
Distorting scripture to abandon jihad was a core tactic of Ghulam Ahmad to placate the British and undermine Islamic resistance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your life are you tempted to reinterpret clear commands of Allah to fit your desires or to gain approval from those around you? How can you protect yourself from this distortion?
?
Ghulam Ahmad justified abrogating jihad by praising the British for their 'noble stance.' What praise from the world are you chasing that might lead you to compromise your commitment to Allah's law?
?
The passage says he 'began to distort as he wished.' Is there any teaching of Islam that you have twisted to make it more comfortable for yourself? What would it cost you to submit fully?

The Divine Punishment and the Colonial Plot Unmasked
Buti narrates Ghulam Ahmad's death as divine punishment and reveals the colonial backing of the sect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of Ghulam Ahmad's ignominious death as divine punishment and Buti's warning about the role of colonial powers in promoting false sects.

Core Idea
God's judgment came upon the false prophet in the most humiliating way, revealing the truth.

After years of deception, Ghulam Ahmad met a humiliating end: he died of cholera in a toilet. Buti presents this as a clear sign from Allah. He then discusses how the sect continued with British support, and he concludes by revealing the true purpose of his narrative: to expose how enemies of Islam sponsor false movements. This lesson focuses on the divine retribution and the political lesson.

Guided Path
1
Read the account of his death
Read the Arabic describing how he died of cholera in a toilet, falling on his face. Reflect on the imagery.
Buti calls it a lesson for those of insight.
2
Understand the continuation of the sect
His successors tried to spread the delusions, with British patronage.
Buti mentions temples and activities given to them.
3
Grasp the author's purpose
Buti states he is not refuting the sect (its falsehood is obvious) but showing how an enemy of Islam stands behind false movements.
This is the key takeaway.
4
Reflect on Britain's role
Buti claims Britain excelled in plotting against Islam. Consider why this is important for Muslims today.
Historical context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And he made a cemetery which he called the cemetery of Paradise; whoever is buried in it is among the people of Paradise. And he called his wives the Mothers of the Believers. And he began gathering around him partisans and followers by every trick and means, with British colonialism behind him pushing and nurturing him. Then he announced that the outward meanings of the Book and the Sunnah are diverted to metaphors, metonymies, and figurative speech. So he began to distort as he wished in the law of the Book and the Sunnah and their rulings. Among his guidance in that was that jihad is abrogated and superseded, especially with respect to the English, because of their noble stance toward the Muslims and their good care for them!! And he continued in that state, claiming prophethood and lying about God and His prophets, and presenting himself to the people as the Messiah Jesus son of Mary, until the decree of God Almighty struck him with cholera (the disease of cholera) and he died in a toilet, falling on his face in the most wretched state and ugliest sight. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that false sects arise only from ignorance, but Buti argues they are often deliberately sponsored by enemies of Islam.
Correction: The passage shows that British colonialism actively supported Ghulam Ahmad's movement, providing resources and recognition.

Checkpoint
What does Buti state as the main purpose of his discussion about the Qadiani sect?
A) To refute their false beliefs with detailed arguments
B) To show how an enemy of Islam supports such false sects
C) To explain the correct understanding of jihad
D) To describe the life of Ghulam Ahmad in detail

Key Takeaway
The ignominious death of the false prophet and the ongoing support from colonial powers reveal that false sects are often tools of external enemies to weaken Islam from within.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see false religious movements gaining followers today, do you recognize the hand of external enemies behind them? How will you investigate before forming an opinion?
?
Allah struck down a false prophet in the most humiliating way. Does this give you confidence that truth always prevails? What does this demand from you when you feel overwhelmed by falsehood?
?
Buti points out that Britain supported this sect. Are there any modern ideologies or groups you follow that might be secretly backed by those hostile to Islam? What steps will you take to ensure your allegiance is to Allah alone?
